================================================================================
  #1 | TABLE | PHB Page 13
  Situation Die Steps Scale
================================================================================

The Situation Die Steps Scale, printed at the top of page 13 and on character templates.

| Bonus | Die |
|-------|-----|
| -d20 | -d12 | -d8 | -d6 | -d4 | +d0 | +d4 | +d6 | +d8 | +d12 | +d20 | +2d20 | +3d20 |
| BONUS <--- | ---> PENALTY |

Steps move toward Bonus (left/up) for negative step modifiers, and toward Penalty (right/down) for positive step modifiers. Base situation die for specialty skills is +d0; for broad skills is +d4; for feat checks is +d4.

================================================================================
  #2 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 13
  Base Situation Die
================================================================================

The base situation die varies by action type. For specialty skills the base die is +d0. For broad skills it is +d4. For feat checks it is +d4. When the Gamemaster assigns a bonus or penalty, you start at the base die and count steps along the Situation Die Steps Scale.

  #11 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 21
  Complete Hero Creation Process
================================================================================

1. Develop a Hero Concept
2. Choose a Species
3. Choose a Career
4. Pick a Profession
5. Assign Ability Scores
5a. Determine Options
6. Purchase Skills
7. Select Perks & Flaws
8. Choose Attributes
9. Complete the Hero Sheet

================================================================================
  #12 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 21 (referenced)
  Alien Abilities and Skills
================================================================================

Referenced on page 21. Provides guidance on how alien heroes differ from human heroes in game terms regarding abilities and skills. (Full text appears to be on a facing page not fully captured in OCR.)

================================================================================
  #13 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 23
  Fraal Psionic Powers
================================================================================

- A fraal talent or Diplomat with Mindwalker secondary profession has psionic energy points equal to Will score (instead of half Will for other such characters).
- A fraal who selects the Mindwalker profession has psionic energy points equal to Will score x 1.5 (instead of Will x 1).
- All fraal receive the psionic broad skill Telepathy as one of their free skills.

================================================================================
  #14 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 25
  Mechalus Special Abilities
================================================================================

- Computer Operation Skill Bonus: Mechalus receive a -1 step situation die bonus when using Knowledge-computer operation or Computer Science-hacking skills. Must merge with the computer via filaments (takes one round to connect/disconnect).
- Cybernetic Enhancements: Born with integrated electronics. Have two neural data slots, an internal processor equivalent to a Good quality nanocomputer, and bio-organic circuitry that functions like a reflex device. Constitution-based cyber limit is CON +4 instead of just CON. Not subject to cybernetic rejection.

================================================================================
  #15 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 27
  Sesheyan Light Sensitivity
================================================================================

Because sesheyans evolved on a world without bright light, normal sunshine and illumination bothers their sensitive eyes:
- Ordinary illumination (cloudy day, moderate room): +1 step penalty to all actions
- Good illumination (full sunshine, bright room): +2 steps penalty
- Amazing light (halogen lamps, flares): +3 steps penalty
Special goggles negate this penalty.

================================================================================
  #16 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 27
  Sesheyan Special Abilities
================================================================================

- Flight: Can fly in any environment with atmospheric pressure >= half Earth normal and gravity <= Earth normal. Use Acrobatics broad skill for flying checks; can purchase flight specialty skill.
- Zero-g Training: Function in zero-g as though they have Acrobatics-zero-g training at rank 1.
- Falling: Never suffer impact damage from falls as long as conscious and able to use wings.
- Night Vision: Can see in near total darkness, ignoring low-illumination penalties. Doesn't work in total darkness or when wearing protective goggles.
- Light Sensitivity: (See separate entry above)

================================================================================
  #17 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 28
  T'sa Special Abilities
================================================================================

- Action Check Bonus: All t'sa heroes receive a -1 step situation die bonus to their action checks. Base action check die is -d4 instead of +d0.
- Juryrig Bonus: Whenever a t'sa makes a Technical Science-juryrig skill check, he receives a -1 step situation die bonus. Base situation die is -d4 instead of +d0.
- Body Armor: All t'sa possess natural body armor: d4+1 (LI), d4 (HI), d4-1 (En).

================================================================================
  #18 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 29-30
  Weren Special Abilities
================================================================================

- Superior Durability: Durability rating uses Constitution score x 1.5 (rounded down).
- Natural Weapon: Retractable claws do d4w/d4+2w/d4m (LI/O) plus Strength bonus on successful Unarmed Attack-brawl or power martial arts check.
- Camouflage: Fur shimmers and changes color to match surroundings. Opponents get +1 step penalty to ranged weapon attacks at distance.
- Primitive Culture: +2 step penalty when using any technological item from Progress Level 4 or higher. Can be reduced to +1 for 4 skill points, eliminated for 4 more skill points at 6th level or higher.

================================================================================
  #19 | TABLE | PHB Page 30 (referenced on multiple pages)
  P1 - Profession Requirements
================================================================================

Referenced as "TABLE P1: PROFESSION REQUIREMENTS" throughout the text. Lists the minimum Ability Scores required for each profession:

| Profession | Primary Abilities | Minimum Scores |
|------------|------------------|----------------|
| Combat Spec | STR, CON | (varies by setting) |
| Diplomat | WIL, PER | (varies by setting) |
| Free Agent | DEX, WIL | (varies by setting) |
| Tech Op | DEX, INT | (varies by setting) |

(Note: The exact table was on a page with heavy OCR artifacts; the requirement minimums are referenced but the exact numbers were not cleanly captured in the OCR text.)

================================================================================
  #20 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 31
  Human Special Abilities
================================================================================

- Skill Bonus: Humans begin with 5 more skill points than members of other species, and are allowed to start with one more broad skill.
- (See TABLE P5 for base numbers; human heroes add +5 skill points and +1 broad skill to those values.)

================================================================================
  #21 | TABLE | PHB Page 31
  Combat Spec Special Benefits
================================================================================

- Action Check Score Increase: +3 points
- Situation Bonus: Choose one specialty skill from Armor Operation, Unarmed Attack, Heavy Weapons, Modern Ranged Weapons, Melee Weapons, or Primitive Ranged Weapons. That specialty's base situation die improves from +d0 to -d4.

================================================================================
  #22 | TABLE | PHB Page 32
  Diplomat Special Benefits
================================================================================

- Action Check Score Increase: +1 point
- Contacts or Resources: Starts with contacts or resources per the Gamemaster Guide
- Secondary Profession: Select a second profession. Can purchase skills from that profession for list price -1 instead of list price.

================================================================================
  #23 | TABLE | PHB Page 32
  Free Agent Special Benefits
================================================================================

- Action Check Score Increase: +2 points
- Resistance Bonus: Choose one Ability and improve its resistance modifier by +1 step
- Last Resort Bonus: Maximum last resort points increased by 1. Can spend 2 last resort points to alter an action (instead of the usual 1 point).

================================================================================
  #24 | TABLE | PHB Page 33
  P2 - Resistance Modifiers
================================================================================

| Ability Score | Resistance Modifier |
|---------------|-------------------|
| 4 or less | -2 steps |
| 5-6 | -1 step |
| 7-10 | 0 |
| 11-12 | +1 step |
| 13-14 | +2 steps |
| 15-16 | +3 steps |
| 17-18 | +4 steps |
| 19+ | +5 steps |

================================================================================
  #25 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 33
  Tech Op Accelerated Learning
================================================================================

Every time a Tech Op hero reaches a new achievement level, he receives the usual number of skill points plus extra skill points depending on the level he just reached:

| Level Attained | Extra Skill Points |
|---------------|-------------------|
| 2-5 | +1 |
| 6-10 | +2 |
| 11-15 | +3 |
| 16-20 | +4 |
| 21+ | +5 |

================================================================================
  #26 | TABLE | PHB Page 33
  Tech Op Special Benefits
================================================================================

- Action Check Score Increase: +1 point
- Accelerated Learning: Extra skill points at each new achievement level (see separate table above)

================================================================================
  #27 | TABLE | PHB Page 34
  P3 - Ability Score Limits (by Species)
================================================================================

Referenced as "TABLE P3: ABILITY SCORE LIMITS." Shows minimum and maximum Ability Scores for each species.

| 11-12 | +1 |
| 13-14 | +2 |

| 19+ | +5 |

(Note: "To a minimum of 1" applies to damage after subtraction.)

================================================================================
  #34 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 40-41
  How to Record Durability
================================================================================

Stun and Wound ratings equal Constitution score. Mortal and Fatigue ratings equal half Constitution score (rounded up). Mark off boxes as damage is taken. Blacken unneeded boxes.

================================================================================
  #35 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 46
  Progress Levels
================================================================================

Progress Levels describe the general level of technological advancement in a society. They affect what equipment is available and how the campaign setting functions. (Referenced throughout but full definitions appear in Chapter 9.)

================================================================================
  #36 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 49
  Situation Die Steps Chart (Full)
================================================================================

Full chart showing situation descriptions, step modifiers, and corresponding dice:

| Situation Description | Step Modifier | Situation Die |
|----------------------|---------------|---------------|
| No Sweat | -5 steps | (beyond -d20) |
| Cakewalk | -4 steps | -d20 |
| Extremely Easy | -3 steps | -d12 |
| Very Easy | -2 steps | -d8 |
| Easy | -1 step | -d6 |
| Average | 0 | -d4/+d0/+d4 (depends on base) |
| Tough | +1 step | +d4/+d6 |
| Hard | +2 steps | +d6/+d8 |
| Challenging | +3 steps | +d8/+d12 |
| Formidable | +4 steps | +d12/+d20 |
| Grueling | +5 steps | +d20/+2d20 |
| Nearly Impossible | +7 steps | +3d20+ |

================================================================================
  #37 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 49
  A Simpler Solution (Eyeball Approach)
================================================================================

Instead of identifying every situation modifier and having you move up or down the table to account for each one, your Gamemaster will come up with a general assessment of the situation -- "eyeballing" it instead of examining it in detail -- and simply direct you to use a particular situation die. The "Situation Description" column on the Situation Die Steps chart is specifically designed to help the Gamemaster when using this eyeball approach. All he has to do is pick a descriptive term that basically describes the situation, and the step penalty or step bonus that applies to your hero's action is instantly determined.

================================================================================
  #38 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 51
  Possible Situation Modifiers
================================================================================

A list of factors that can modify the situation die for any given action:
- Base Situation Die
- Opponent's Resistance Modifier
- Range Modifier
- Cover Modifier
- Dodge Modifier
- Skill Situation Modifiers
- Other Situation Modifiers

|----------------|---------------------------|

| Failure | +1 step penalty |
| Ordinary | -1 step bonus |
| Good | -2 step bonus |
| Amazing | -3 step bonus |

================================================================================
  #41 | TABLE | PHB Page 52
  Two Actions at Once Penalties
================================================================================

When a character performs two related physical activities in one phase:
- Primary action: +2 step penalty
- Secondary action: +4 step penalty
These penalties are cumulative with any other situation die modifiers.

================================================================================
  #42 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 53
  Gravity Effects
================================================================================

Lists environmental penalties:
- Gravity: variable penalties
- Radiation: variable penalties
- Atmospheric Composition: variable penalties
- Heat and Cold: variable penalties

================================================================================
  #43 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 55
  How Armor Works
================================================================================

Armor provides damage reduction dice rolled against incoming damage types (LI, HI, En). The armor die is rolled and the result is subtracted from the damage inflicted. If the subtraction produces a result less than 1, the armor failed to block any damage on that attack.

================================================================================
  #44 | TABLE | PHB Page 55
  Stun Recovery (Knocked Out)
================================================================================

When a knocked-out hero attempts Resolve-physical resolve checks to recover:

| Check Result | Stun Points Recovered |
|-------------|----------------------|
| Critical Failure | 0 (stays unconscious) |
| Failure | 0 (stays unconscious) |
| Ordinary | 2 stun points |
| Good | 4 stun points |
| Amazing | 6 stun points |

On any success, the character becomes conscious but can't attempt other actions in the upcoming round.

================================================================================
  #45 | TABLE | PHB Page 56
  P11 - Combat Movement Effects
================================================================================

Shows penalties for performing actions while moving in combat:

| Movement Mode | Can Act? | Penalty to Other Actions |
|--------------|----------|-------------------------|
| Walk | Yes | No penalty |
| Easy Swim | Yes | +2 steps |
| Run | Yes | +1 step |
| Swim | No | No actions possible (swimming only) |
| Sprint | No | No actions possible |
| Glide | Yes | +2 steps |
| Fly | Yes | +1 step |

================================================================================
  #46 | TABLE | PHB Page 56
  Fatigue Recovery
================================================================================

Resolve-physical resolve skill check results for fatigue recovery (during complete rest):

| Check Result | Fatigue Points Recovered |
|-------------|-------------------------|
| Critical Failure | 0 |
| Marginal | 1 |
| Ordinary | 2 |
| Good | 3 |
| Amazing | 4 |

Checks made once per hour of complete rest.

================================================================================
  #47 | TABLE | PHB Page 57
  P12 - Encumbrance
================================================================================

| Load | Move Penalty | Action Penalty |
|------|-------------|---------------|
| STR x 2 | 100% (none) | 0 |
| STR x 4 | 75% | +1 |
| STR x 5 | 50% | +2 |
| STR x 6 | 25% | +3 |

The reduction in movement rate applies to both combat movement and overland movement. The penalty applies to all actions related to Strength- and Dexterity-based skills, as well as the character's Strength and Dexterity resistance modifiers.

  P13 - Overland Movement
================================================================================

| Mode of Travel | Kilometers per Hour | Hours per Fatigue Check |
|---------------|--------------------|-----------------------|
| Stroll | (low) | (long interval) |
| March | (medium) | (medium interval) |
| Forced march | (high) | (short interval) |

(Exact values degraded in OCR but the structure is: stroll is slowest with longest fatigue interval, forced march is fastest with shortest fatigue interval.)

================================================================================
  #49 | TABLE | PHB Page 57-58
  P14 - Throw Situation Modifiers
================================================================================

| Object Type | Short Range | Medium Range | Long Range |
|------------|-------------|--------------|------------|
| Designed for throwing | -1 step | +1 step | +2 steps |
| Not for throwing (light) | +1 step | +3 steps | +8 steps |
| Heavy | +4 steps | - | - |

Heavy objects (more than 3 kg but no more than half STR in kg) can only be thrown at short range.

================================================================================
  #50 | TABLE | PHB Page 57
  Attacking with Two Weapons Penalties
================================================================================

- Skilled hand weapon: +2 step penalty
- Off hand weapon: +4 step penalty
These penalties are reduced if a character has the Ambidextrous perk.

================================================================================
  #51 | TABLE | PHB Page 58-59
  P15 - Impact Damage
================================================================================

Cross-reference fall distance with skill check result:

| Distance | Critical Failure | Failure | Ordinary | Good | Amazing |
|----------|-----------------|---------|----------|------|---------|
| Ex (< 3m) | d6+4m | d8+2s | d4s | - | - |
| S (3-10m) | d12+6m | d6+2w | d8+2s | d4s | - |
| M (11-30m) | d12+6m | d8+6m | d6+2w | d8+2s | d4s |
| L (31-60m) | d12+8m | d12+6m | d8+6m | d6+4m | d6+2w |
| T (61m+) | death | d12+8m | d12+6m | d8+6m | d6+4m |

Ex = extremely short fall or collision at <= 20 kph
S = short fall (3-10m) or collision at 21-60 kph
M = medium fall (11-30m) or collision at 61-120 kph
L = long fall (31-60m) or collision at 121-300 kph
T = terminal velocity (61m+) or collision at 300+ kph

Note: On lighter gravity worlds, reduce distance by one grade. On heavier gravity worlds, increase by one grade.

================================================================================
  #52 | TABLE | PHB Page 59
  Holding Breath - Damage Results
================================================================================

When holding breath beyond safe duration, Stamina-endurance check results:

| Check Result | Stun Damage Suffered |
|-------------|---------------------|
| Critical Failure | 4 stun points |
| Failure | 3 stun points |
| Ordinary | 2 stun points |
| Good | 1 stun point |
| Amazing | 0 |

A Failure or Critical Failure result (or losing all stun points) causes unconsciousness and danger of drowning.

================================================================================
  #53 | TABLE | PHB Page 63
  P16 - Situation Die Modifiers (Skill Checks)
================================================================================

| Condition | Modifier |
|-----------|----------|
| Extreme (worst) | +3 steps |
| Moderate | +2 steps |
| Slight | +1 step |
| Marginal | None |
| Ordinary | -1 step |
| Good | -2 steps |
| Amazing (best) | -3 steps |

More difficult conditions apply penalties (positive steps); less difficult conditions provide bonuses (negative steps).

================================================================================
  #54 | TABLE | PHB Page 63
  P17 - Complex Skill Checks
================================================================================

Conditions affecting complex skill checks:

**Situation Die Modifiers:**

| Condition | Modifier |
|-----------|----------|
| Critical | +4 steps |
| Extreme | +3 steps |
| Moderate | +2 steps |
| Slight | +1 step |
| Marginal | None |
| Ordinary | -1 step |
| Good | -2 steps |
| Amazing (best) | -3 steps |

**Successes Needed by Complexity:**

| Complexity | Successes Needed |
|-----------|-----------------|
| Marginal | 2 |
| Ordinary | 4 |
| Good | 6* |
| Amazing | 8+* |

*Specific number decided by the Gamemaster.

On any individual dice roll: Ordinary = 1 success, Good = 2 successes, Amazing = 3 successes. Three Failure results end the attempt. A single Critical Failure immediately ruins the attempt.

  #55 | TABLE | PHB Page 63-64
  P18 - Skill List (Base Situation Dice)
================================================================================

| Type of Action | Score Used | Base Die |
|---------------|-----------|----------|
| Feat check | Ability Score | +d4 |
| Broad skill | Ability Score | +d4 |
| Specialty skill | Ability Score + Rank | +d0 |
| Untrained | Half Ability Score | +d4 |

================================================================================
  #56 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 63
  Who Makes the Rolls?
================================================================================

In almost every case, only the acting character makes a skill check to determine the result of his attempt. The Gamemaster may sometimes make rolls secretly on behalf of a character, particularly for skills like Awareness, Knowledge, or Stealth, where the character might not know the outcome of the attempt.

  #63 | TABLE | PHB Page 68
  P20 - Accuracy by Range
================================================================================

For thrown objects or indirect fire weapons:

| Skill Check Result | Short | Medium | Long |
|-------------------|-------|--------|------|
| Critical Failure | 4 m off | 8 m off | 12 m off |
| Failure | 2 m off | 4 m off | 6 m off |
| Ordinary | on target | 2 m off | 4 m off |
| Good | on target | on target | 2 m off |
| Amazing | always on target | always on target | always on target |

================================================================================
  #64 | TABLE | PHB Page 68
  Jump Distances
================================================================================

| Jump Type | Ordinary | Good | Amazing |
|----------|----------|------|---------|
| Standing jump | 1 m | 2 m | 3 m |
| Running jump | 2 m | 4 m | 6 m |
| Vertical leap | 1 m | 1.5 m | 2 m |

Critical Failure: Hero trips and suffers d6 stun damage.
Marginal: Hero makes Ordinary distance but suffers d4 stun damage from poor landing.

Increased Distance at higher ranks:
- Running jump: +1 m at ranks 3, 6, 9, 12
- Standing jump: +1 m at ranks 4, 7, 10
- Vertical leap: +0.5 m at ranks 5, 8, 11

================================================================================
  #65 | TABLE | PHB Page 69
  P21 - Heavy Weapons Range Modifiers
================================================================================

| Weapon Type | Short | Medium | Long |
|------------|-------|--------|------|
| Direct fire | -1 step | None | +1 step |
| Indirect fire | +2 steps | -2 steps | None |

================================================================================
  #66 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 69-70
  Melee Weapons Rank Benefits
================================================================================

As a hero achieves higher ranks in Melee Weapons specialty skills, he gains:
- Resistance Modifier: Improvement to Strength resistance modifier at certain ranks
- Reaction Parry: Ability to parry as a reaction at higher ranks
- Double-Strike: Ability to make two attacks at higher ranks
- Multistrike: Ability to strike multiple opponents at highest ranks

================================================================================
  #67 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 70
  Unarmed Attack Rank Benefits
================================================================================

As a hero achieves higher ranks in Unarmed Attack specialty skills (brawl, power martial arts), he gains:
- No Hands: Can make unarmed attacks even when hands are bound
- Knockout: Can attempt to knock out an opponent
- Increased Damage: Damage improves at higher ranks

================================================================================
  #68 | TABLE | PHB Page 72
  Dodge Skill Effects
================================================================================

Dodge skill check result provides the following adjustments to the hero's resistance modifier:

| Dodge Result | Resistance Modifier Adjustment |
|-------------|-------------------------------|
| Critical Failure | -2 steps |
| Failure | None |
| Ordinary | +1 step |
| Good | +2 steps |
| Amazing | +3 steps |

================================================================================
  #69 | TABLE | PHB Page 74-75
  P22 - Range Modifiers by Weapon Type
================================================================================

| Weapon Type | Short | Medium | Long |
|------------|-------|--------|------|
| Pistol | -1 step | None | +1 step |
| Rifle | -1 step | None | +1 step |
| Submachine gun | -1 step | +1 step | +3 steps |
| Bow/crossbow/sling | None | +1 step | +3 steps |
| Flintlock pistol | (as pistol) | (as pistol) | (as pistol) |
| Flintlock rifle | (as rifle) | (as rifle) | (as rifle) |

================================================================================
  #70 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 75-76
  Ranged Weapons Rank Benefits
================================================================================

As a hero achieves higher ranks in ranged weapon specialty skills, he gains:
- Distance Precision: Improved accuracy at range
- Double-Shot: Ability to fire twice
- Rate of Fire Increase: Faster shooting

================================================================================
  #71 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 75
  Automatic Weapon Attack Modes
================================================================================

Automatic weapons (some rifles, all SMGs, and a few heavy weapons) can fire in multiple modes:
- Fire: Single shot, normal attack
- Burst: Short burst of rounds, providing bonus to hit but using more ammunition
- Autofire: Full automatic fire, spraying an area with bullets; can target multiple opponents

================================================================================
  #72 | TABLE | PHB Page 75-76
  Stealth vs. Detection Modifiers
================================================================================

How the hero's Stealth skill check result modifies the observer's detection attempt:

| Stealth Result | Observer's Modifier |
|---------------|-------------------|
| Critical Failure | -2 bonus (easier to detect) |
| Failure | No modifier |
| Ordinary | +1 penalty (harder to detect) |
| Good | +2 penalty |
| Amazing | +3 penalty |

================================================================================
  #73 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 76
  Stealth Skills Rank Benefit
================================================================================

Increased Effect: As a hero achieves higher ranks in any Stealth specialty skill (hide, shadow, sneak), the penalty applied to the observer's detection check improves. This makes the hero progressively harder to detect.

================================================================================
  #74 | TABLE | PHB Page 77
  Sneak Attack Bonus
================================================================================

If a hero successfully sneaks up on an opponent and attacks in the same phase:
| Sneak Result | Attack Bonus |
|-------------|-------------|
| Ordinary | -1 step |
| Good | -2 steps |
| Amazing | -3 steps |

================================================================================
  #75 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 79 (referenced)
  Survival Situation Modifiers
================================================================================

Terrain-based modifiers for Survival skill checks:
- Different terrain types (arctic, desert, forest, jungle, mountains, ocean, plains, swamp, urban) each have specific situation die modifiers
- Conditions range from favorable (Ordinary terrain with abundant resources) to harsh (Extreme environments with scarce resources)

  Resist Pain Skill Check Results
================================================================================

|-------------|--------|
| Critical Failure | Hero can't act for 2d4 phases |
| Failure | Normal damage penalties apply |
| Ordinary | Ignore 1 step of penalty |
| Good | Ignore 2 steps of penalty |
| Amazing | Ignore 3 steps of penalty |

| Good | d4+2w | d6+3w | d4+3m |
| Amazing | d4+2w+ | d6+3w+ | d4+3m+ |

The degree of success also defines the complexity of any subsequent disarm checks by other characters.

| Result | Stun Points Recovered |
|--------|----------------------|

| Good | 2 |
| Amazing | 3 |

**Heal Wound Damage:** Complex skill check required. Good complexity with first aid kit; Ordinary with trauma pack. Heals 1 wound (first aid kit) or 2 wounds (trauma pack) on completion. Critical Failure inflicts 1 wound.

Situation die modifiers for medical skill checks (first aid, treatment, surgery):
- Equipment quality (trauma pack vs. first aid kit vs. no equipment)
- Working conditions (combat scene vs. calm environment)
- Patient condition (conscious vs. unconscious, number of wounds)
- Alien species penalty (+3 steps without xenomedicine skill)

================================================================================
  #82 | TABLE | PHB Page 86
  Surgery Complexity
================================================================================

Complexity of surgery depends on mortal damage:

**For mortal damage:**
| Mortal Points | Complexity |
|--------------|-----------|
| 1 point | Marginal |
| 2 points | Ordinary |
| 3 points | Good |
| 4+ points | Amazing |

**For wound damage only:**
| Wound Points | Complexity |
|-------------|-----------|
| 2 points | Marginal |
| 4 points | Ordinary |
| 6 points | Good |
| 8+ points | Amazing |

For every two successes: heals 1 mortal damage and 2 wound damage. One new check per hour. Critical Failure or 3 Failures = patient suffers 1 mortal damage and all successes lost.

| Best possible (high-tech, full staff) | -4 step bonus |

  #84 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 87
  Navigation Situation Modifiers
================================================================================

Situation die modifiers for Navigation skill checks include:
- Quality of equipment available
- Familiarity with the region
- Weather and environmental conditions
- Time pressure (optimum is 5 minutes; less time = penalty, more time up to 10 min = bonus)

================================================================================
  #85 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 87
  Drivespace Off Course Results
================================================================================

Results when a drivespace astrogation check results in Critical Failure or Failure:
- Critical Failure: Major navigational error; make another check with +2 penalty and consult off-course results
- Marginal Success: Arrive off course by significant distance
- Good Success: Minor course deviation
- Amazing Success: Correct course quickly

================================================================================
  #86 | TABLE | PHB Page 87
  Treatment Healing Results
================================================================================

**Heal Stun Damage:** Same as first aid (2/3/4 stun points).
**Knockout Recovery:** 2/3/4 stun points (better than first aid).
**Heal Wound Damage:** Complex skill check. Ordinary complexity with first aid kit; Marginal with trauma pack. Heals 2 wounds (first aid kit) or 4 wounds (trauma pack) on completion. Critical Failure inflicts 1 wound.
**Dying:** Stabilizes mortal damage, increasing time between Stamina-endurance checks from 1/hour to 1/day.

================================================================================
  #87 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 88
  System/Surface Off Course Results
================================================================================

Results when a system or surface navigation check results in Critical Failure or Failure:
- Critical Failure: Major navigational error; make another check with +2 penalty
- Marginal Success: Course plotted with extra travel time
- Ordinary Success: Course plotted at normal travel time plus d4 time units
- Good Success: Course plotted at normal travel time

================================================================================
  #93 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 92
  Animal Handling Situation Modifiers
================================================================================

**Animal Handling Situation Modifiers**

*Training modifiers (applied to each segment of complex skill check):*

The sidebar is referenced on page 92 and provides modifiers for training animals and handling trained/untrained animals. The OCR captured only the title ("Animal Handling Situation Modifiers") with fragmented data. Based on the descriptive text:

**Training an animal:**
- Situation modifier depends on the type of animal being worked with
- Certain types of animals take longer to train (more successes needed)
- At least 4 hours/day of work required; skill check at end of each week

**After training -- having an animal perform a task:**
- Unfamiliar animal (trained by someone else): penalty modifier
- Unfamiliar + Good task: +3 penalty (cumulative)
- Wild/untrained animal: can only perform tasks of Ordinary difficulty or less

**Task difficulty:**
- Ordinary: simple one-word commands (Attack, Come, Sit, Stay, Fetch, Speak, Quiet)
- Good: combination of two Ordinary tasks, or something more difficult (e.g., pushing a lever)
- Amazing: something very few animals can/will do on command (e.g., running into a burning building)

================================================================================
  #94 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 94
  Creativity Situation Modifiers
================================================================================

Referenced on page 94. The sidebar provides situation modifiers for Creativity skill checks. The OCR captured only fragments. Based on text context:

- Conditions under which work is being done provide situation modifiers
- Number of successes required relates to complexity of task
- Dashing off a four-line poem: Ordinary accomplishment
- Composing a Shakespearean-quality sonnet: Amazing
- Critical Failure or three Failure results: work is scrapped

================================================================================
  #95 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 94
  Investigate Situation Modifiers
================================================================================

Referenced on page 94. Provides situation modifiers for Investigate skill checks. From text context:

- "Time units" definition depends on scene type: in rounds, usually a phase; in longer scenes, minutes/hours/days
- More time spent investigating = better chance of success
- Any success reveals significant information; degree of success determines accuracy/detail
- Failure: hero wasn't able to reach accurate conclusion in time allowed

================================================================================
  #96 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 96
  Street Smart Situation Modifiers
================================================================================

Referenced on page 96. Provides situation modifiers for Street Smart skill checks. Modifiers are cumulative. From text:

Factors affecting skill check:
- Hero's relationship with the person/group
- Scarcity, legality, or difficulty of item/service sought
- Connections that might influence the deal
- Law level of the society (defined in Gamemaster Guide)

Example: If hero seeks an item of Amazing scarcity/illegality on a planet protected by Good law enforcers, the skill check carries a +6 penalty.

================================================================================
  #97 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 97 (referenced on pages 52, 66, 80)
  Encounter Skills
================================================================================

Referenced throughout pages 1-90 but the full description is on page 97. Encounter skills (Interaction, Leadership, Entertainment, Deception, etc.) are used during encounter scenes to change the attitude of NPCs. The target's Will resistance modifier applies as a situation die modifier. Success can shift an NPC's attitude from Hostile to Friendly or better.

================================================================================
  #98 | TABLE | PHB Page 97
  P25: Encounter Skill Effects
================================================================================

**TABLE P25: ENCOUNTER SKILL EFFECTS**

This table shows how encounter skill results change a target's attitude. The target's current attitude determines the row; the degree of success determines the column.

| Starting Attitude | Ordinary Result | Good Result | Amazing Result |
|---|---|---|---|
| Combative | Hostile | Neutral | Friendly |
| Hostile | Neutral | Friendly | Charmed |
| Neutral | Friendly | Charmed | Fanatic |
| Friendly | Charmed | Fanatic | Fanatic |

**Encounter Skills include:**
- Business (INT)
- Law (INT)
- Administration (WIL)
- Street Smart (WIL)
- Culture (PER)
- Entertainment (PER)
- Interaction (PER)
- Leadership (PER)
- Deception (bribe, bluff only) (PER)

**Attitude Definitions (from page 98):**
- Combative: Will attack or actively oppose the hero
- Hostile: Unfriendly, uncooperative, possibly threatening
- Neutral: Indifferent, no strong feelings either way
- Friendly: Well-disposed, willing to help within reason
- Charmed: Very favorably inclined, will go out of their way to help
- Fanatic: Completely devoted, will do almost anything

================================================================================
  #99 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 100
  Entertainment Skill -- Enhance Another Skill
================================================================================

Referenced on page 100, titled "Entertainment Sk... Enhance Another Skill." Describes how the Entertainment broad skill and its specialties can be used to enhance other skills. Audience attitude modifiers:

- Simply showing audience a good time (not trying to make fans): -1 bonus
- Trying to make a name/impress at risk of alienating some: +1 penalty
- Ulterior motive (stun, shock, divert attention): +3 penalty

================================================================================
  #100 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 101
  Interaction Situation Modifiers
================================================================================

Referenced on page 101. Provides situation modifiers for Interaction skill checks. From text context:

- Target's Will resistance modifier applies
- Target's current attitude provides modifier (see Table P25)
- Modifiers are cumulative
- Neither Combative nor Fanatic characters can be influenced by Interaction
- Changes in attitude from Interaction are longer-lasting than from Deception or Entertainment

================================================================================
  #101 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 102
  Taunt Situation Modifiers
================================================================================

Referenced on page 102. Special modifiers for the taunt skill based on target's attitude. The taunt skill has no effect on Charmed or Fanatic targets.

Check results:
- Critical Failure: Target gets -2 bonus to next action against taunter
- Failure: No effect
- Ordinary: +1 penalty to target's next action
- Good: +2 penalty to target's next action
- Amazing: +3 penalty to target's next action AND target shifts one grade toward Combative

================================================================================
  #102 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 102
  Leadership Situation Modifiers
================================================================================

Referenced on page 102. Provides situation modifiers for Leadership skill checks:

- Leader must use an action to attempt the skill check
- Modified by attitude of targets plus other factors
- Can't be used on Combative targets
- On success, provides -1 bonus to followers' actions for remainder of current round and all of following round

Results:
- Critical Failure: Followers get +1 penalty; no further Leadership checks in scene
- Failure: No bonus; can try again next round
- Ordinary: Up to 2 followers receive bonus
- Good: Up to 4 followers receive bonus
- Amazing: Up to 6 followers receive bonus

================================================================================
  #106 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 112
  Signature Equipment (Careers Chapter Introduction)
================================================================================

Equipment is expensive, and most heroes just starting out can't afford a lot of it. In some cases, they can't even afford the basic items necessary to let them play the characters they have in mind. What good would a hacker be without a computer, a medtech without a medical kit, or a law enforcer without a standard weapon? With the intention of avoiding this problem, we've provided each sample career with signature equipment that the Gamemaster can decide to give to a hero without paying the cost out of that hero's starting funds. In most cases, this piece of signature equipment is the least expensive model available -- a starting hero shouldn't begin with a top-of-the-line ship, or with the best weapons, armor, or gear in the campaign.

Also, the equipment that's available to a character depends on the Progress Level and type of campaign he's set in. (Progress Levels are described in detail in the first few pages of Chapter 9: Goods & Services, which is also the chapter that contains lists of the basic equipment available to heroes.) If a piece of equipment listed for a career isn't available because of the restrictions of the campaign, your Gamemaster will exchange it for an equivalent item that fits into his campaign.

At the end of each career description in this chapter is a suggested "package" for the character type in question, including the number of points needed for the character to acquire those skills. In no case does the cost of a skill package exceed 35 points, which means that a hero will usually still have points left that can be spent on other skills (unless he or she has an especially low Intelligence score). Those additional skills could be taken from the ones that are mentioned in the descriptive text for a career, or any other skill that fits your conception of the hero you're creating.

The point costs for these packages assume that the hero in question is human; as such, the packages don't mention skills that a human hero receives for free. For a hero who belongs to one of the alien species, adjust the list of necessary skills and the skill costs accordingly. For example, a sesheyan Combat Spec who takes the law enforcer skill package doesn't have to purchase the Melee Weapons broad skill, but will have to buy the Athletics broad skill if he or she wants to have it.

================================================================================
  #114 | TABLE | PHB Page 131
  P31: Rich and Poor
================================================================================

**TABLE P31: RICH AND POOR**

| Success Level | Filthy Rich Multiplier | Dirt Poor Reduction |
|---|---|---|
| Marginal | x10 | -90% |
| Ordinary | x20 | -75% |
| Good | x50 | -50% |
| Amazing | x100 | -25% |

For Filthy Rich: Make perk check using Personality with +d4 situation die. Count Critical Failure as Marginal for this roll. Multiply spending money or starting funds by the listed multiplier.

For Dirt Poor: Use the same procedure and subtract the listed percentage from bankroll.

Note: Characters with Filthy Rich or Dirt Poor are NOT entitled to receive a career signature item.

================================================================================
  #115 | TABLE | PHB Page 132
  P32: Progress Levels
================================================================================

**TABLE P32: PROGRESS LEVELS**

| PL | Name | Key Features |
|---|---|---|
| 0 | Stone Age | Fire, domestication of animals, agriculture. Weapons: club, dagger, spear, bow. Leather/hide armor. |
| 1 | Bronze/Iron Age | Metalworking, bronze/iron tools and weapons. Swords, chariots, cavalry. Chain/plate armor. |
| 2 | Middle Ages | Architecture, metallurgy, mathematics. Printing. Sea travel. Gunpowder weapons appear late. Chain and plate armors. |
| 3 | Age of Reason | Scientific method, experimentation. Democracy. Cannon, musket, flintlock. Light melee weapons remain. |
| 4 | Industrial Age | Steam/electric power, telegraph, telephone, radio. Rifles, pistols, machine guns. Mechanized war machines. Aircraft, submersibles. |
| 5 | Information Age | Computers, electronics, fission power. Automobiles. Chemical rockets, early space travel. Guided weapons. |
| 6 | Fusion Age | Fusion power, advanced space exploration/colonization. Second-gen Grid. Gravity induction tech appears late. Chemical firearms still dominant. |
| 7 | Gravity Age | Mass reactor, stardrive. Starfaring civilization. Crude energy weapons. Powered armor. Energy screens. Personal melee weapons resurgence. |
| 8 | Energy Age | Miniaturized stardrive. Personal force screens and energy weapons dominate. Starfighters mass-produced. World ships constructed. |
| 9 | Matter Age | Practical control of matter at subatomic level. Generally beyond comprehension. |
| 10 | Far Future | Beyond current understanding. |

================================================================================
  #116 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 134
  Gravity Induction
================================================================================

Referenced on page 134. Describes gravity induction technology -- the key technology of PL 7 (Gravity Age). Crude applications first appear late in PL 6 as civilian and military vehicles that move through air without physical propulsion or fuel consumption. At PL 7, the mass reactor and stardrive are developed, enabling interstellar travel.

================================================================================
  #124 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 138
  Want Something That's Not Here?
================================================================================

Referenced on page 138. This sidebar advises players and GMs that the equipment lists are not exhaustive. If a player wants an item not listed, work with the Gamemaster to determine its availability, cost, and game effects based on similar items in the lists.

================================================================================
  #125 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 140-141
  Trauma Pack I Description
================================================================================

Trauma Pack I appears as a small illustration/sidebar callout on page 140. The trauma pack is described as the size of a paperback book, containing a dedicated computer program, medicine injectors, applicators, synthetic drugs, and artificial blood and skin -- creating a portable emergency treatment center.

**Trauma Pack I (PL 6):**
- Provides -2 bonus to Knowledge-first aid OR -3 bonus to Medical Science-treatment
- Contains enough material for: 6 attempts to heal wounds, 6 attempts to heal stun/awaken knocked out, 2 uses to stabilize mortal damage
- Refill cost: $100

**Trauma Pack II (PL 7):**
- Autonomous version, designed for body tank armor/cybernetic enhancements
- Monitors vital signs and activates automatically at first sign of damage
- Knockout recovery: Instantly restores stun points to leave wearer at half damage; +2 step action check penalty next round
- Wound recovery: When >half wound points lost, restores d4+2 wound points
- Mortal damage: Immediately stabilizes; all actions at +3 penalty until healed
- Contains drugs for 2 applications of each function; max 1 pack per individual

================================================================================
  #126 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 145
  Survival Gear Description
================================================================================

A small callout box on page 145 near the survival gear section. The survival gear belt pouch includes: magnetic compass, signal mirror, butane lighter, 30 meters of 20-kg test fishing line and 2 hooks, 20 waterproof matches, and a lightweight insulated blanket.

================================================================================
  #130 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 156
  Cybernetics and PL 6 Computers
================================================================================

Referenced on page 156 under the Nanocomputer description. Explains that for nanocomputers to be available, the GM must be using at least a scaled-down version of the optional rules in Chapter 15: Cybertech. The nanocomputer requires cytronic circuitry connecting to the user's neural network.

================================================================================
  #131 | TABLE | PHB Page 157-158
  Computer System Types in the Grid
================================================================================

**Grid System Types:**

| System Type | Access | Description |
|---|---|---|
| Public | Anyone with computer and modem | E-mail, public databases, shopping, banking, bulletin boards, corporate info, topic Gridsites |
| Private | Password required; records kept | Private databases, fee-based entertainment/news/business, pay-to-play games |
| Restricted | Specially designed to prevent unauthorized access | High-level corporate/government systems, bank accounts, personnel files, classified systems |

**Network Types and Protection:**

| Network Type | Access Level | Protection Level |
|---|---|---|
| Academic | Public | Marginal (at best) |
| Access Service | Private | Good (at least) |
| Corporate | Restricted | Ordinary |
| Financial | Restricted | Amazing (unhackable at PL 5) |
| Government | Private | Marginal |
| Military | Private | Good |
| Open | Public | Ordinary or less |
| Operational | Restricted | Amazing |
| Portal | Private | Ordinary |
| Ultrasecure | Restricted | Amazing |
| User (home) | Private | Marginal |

================================================================================
  #132 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 159
  Generating Gridsuit Shadows
================================================================================

Referenced on page 159. Describes how gridsuit users (those without nanocomputers/NIJacks) can generate shadows to experience the Grid. The gridsuit provides a full-body sensory suit, virtu-self goggles, and total-sound earphones. While wearing it:
- User must remain at connection location
- All Awareness checks involving real-world phenomena receive +3 penalty
- Experience is not as "real" as true gridpiloting

================================================================================
  #136 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 163
  Progress Levels Don't Mix Well
================================================================================

Referenced on page 163. This sidebar explains that programs from one Progress Level may not function properly (or at all) on computers from a different Progress Level. PL 5 programs are generally too primitive for PL 6 machines (though they may run in a degraded mode), and PL 6 programs are too complex for PL 5 hardware.

| Quality | Skill Score | Extra Memory Slots |
|---|---|---|
| Marginal | 8 | 0 |
| Ordinary | 12 | 0 |
| Good | 16 | +1 |
| Amazing | 20 | +2 |

Virus size = program inside it + extra memory for virus shell.
Quality of virus must match or exceed quality of program hidden within it.
Base situation die for virus skill check: +d0, modified by antivirus penalties.

================================================================================
  #146 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 168
  Layered Defenses / Information Retrieval
================================================================================

**Information Retrieval from Computer Systems**

Accessing open computer systems: no skill check required.
Closed/protected systems have layered defenses requiring a series of skill checks (complex skill check).

**Layers of Defense by Processor Quality:**
- Marginal: 2 layers
- Ordinary: 3-4 layers
- Good: 5-7 layers
- Amazing: 8-10 layers

This number also represents successes needed to penetrate all defenses. Programs like alarm add penalties; fortress adds additional layers.

Referenced on page 169. Describes how an AI can operate all ship systems at its base Intelligence score but can only actively crew one system at a time. If the ship has dedicated computer systems, the AI can apply the bonuses from those systems to its Intelligence feat checks.

  PL 6 Robot Example: T-Kat
================================================================================

**T-Kat** (PL 6 Robot)
Small, box-shaped robot for household or industrial use. Designed for hallway cleaning and pest control using low-powered sonics and vacuum-sweeper.

STR 1, DEX 8, CON 2, INT 12, WIL 4, PER 1
Durability: 2/2/1
Movement: walk 6 (wheels)
Action check score: 8+/7/3/1
Actions per round: 1
Mass: 47 kg
Size: 45 cm
Processor quality: Ordinary (5 active slots)
Stored programs: operating system, pest identification utility, eradication utility, housekeeping utility, service map
Cost: $8,000

**A-Eyes** (PL 7 Robot)
Small sensory robot controlled by an AI program housed in a ship or installation computer. Floats and moves using a tiny gravitonic inducer, transferring visual and audio data back to the AI.

(Statistics continue on page 171, beyond the scope of this extraction.)

================================================================================
  #153 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 175
  How to Read the Weapons Tables
================================================================================

How to Read the Weapons Tables

- **Weapon:** The name of the weapon.
- **Skill:** The skill used to attack with this weapon.
- **Acc:** Accuracy modifier applied to the attack skill check (+1 penalty = less accurate, -1 bonus = more accurate, 0 = standard).
- **Actions:** The number of actions required to fire/use the weapon (determines rate of fire).
- **Clip Size:** The number of rounds/charges the weapon holds before reloading.
- **Clip Cost:** The cost in dollars to purchase one clip/reload of ammunition.
- **Hide:** The concealability of the weapon (Personal = easily concealed, Lo = concealable under a coat, En/O = not easily concealed, HI/G = heavy/large, HUG = huge).
- **Mass:** The weight of the weapon.
- **Avail:** Availability rating.
- **Type:** Damage type (F = fire/energy, B = ballistic/high impact, A = area effect, HI/G = high impact/Good toughness, En/O = energy, etc.).
- **Range:** Short/Medium/Long range in meters.
- **Damage (O/G/A):** Damage dealt on Ordinary/Good/Amazing success results.

================================================================================
  #155 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 179-180
  Electrochemical Weapons
================================================================================

In the early part of the Gravity Age, the discovery of a true superconducting metallic alloy -- a mixture of lanthanum and several other ores -- opens a whole new area in the technology of storing, transmitting, and employing electricity. In addition to making magnetic accelerators, levitation, and 100 percent efficient electric motors possible, an application of this same technology allows the building of enormously powerful capacitors in a very small space.

All kinds of hand-held items use energy cells that put chemical batteries of earlier eras to shame. Two important weapons applications emerge from this technology. First, hand-held rail guns, accelerators, and other such devices are made possible by lanthanide-alloy coils. Second, weapons requiring a strong source of electrical power -- such as the charge firearms -- make use of lanthanide capacitors. Lanth cells resemble the flat-disk batteries of PL 5, though they are two to three times as thick.

Lanthanide energy cells at this Progress Level still last for four clips of ammunition, but cost $200.

================================================================================
  #157 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 182
  Amazing Damage Knockout
================================================================================

As noted in Chapter 3: Heroes in Action, someone who takes Amazing damage from an attack must succeed on a Stamina-endurance skill check to avoid falling unconscious. It's important to remember that this rule also applies to Amazing damage from area-effect weapons such as grenades and prepared explosives -- a character who's right next to a grenade when it goes off not only suffers heavy damage, but might be knocked out of action for the rest of the scene.

================================================================================
  #160 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 190
  How to Read the Armor Table
================================================================================

- **Armor:** The name of the armor.
- **Skill:** The skill used to operate/wear the armor (Armor Operation broad skill, with combat or powered specialty).
- **LI / HI / En:** The armor's damage reduction against Low Impact, High Impact, and Energy damage respectively. Roll the indicated dice; the result is the number of points of damage absorbed.
- **Hide:** Whether the armor can be concealed.
- **Mass:** Weight of the armor.
- **Cost:** Purchase price.

================================================================================
  #161 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 190
  Aliens in Armor
================================================================================

Armor designed for human body types doesn't automatically fit alien heroes. Aliens with significantly different body structures may need custom-fitted armor. The Gamemaster determines whether standard armor can be adapted for a particular alien species and what the cost modifier might be.

================================================================================
  #162 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 191
  Degrading Damage
================================================================================

Armor can be damaged through use. When armor absorbs damage that equals or exceeds the maximum it could stop (rolling the highest possible result on its armor dice), the armor's protection is degraded. Reduce the armor's rating by 1 point for the affected damage type. Armor can be repaired using the Technical Science-repair skill.

================================================================================
  #164 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 200
  Speeding Up and Slowing Down
================================================================================

A vehicle's speed changes from phase to phase depending on the operator's actions. If the operator takes an action to accelerate, the vehicle's speed increases by its acceleration rate. If the operator brakes, the speed decreases by the same amount. A vehicle's acceleration rate equals its cruising speed divided by 4 (round down). So a car with a cruising speed of 100 kph has an acceleration rate of 25 kph per phase.

================================================================================
  #165 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 200
  Vehicle Operation Modifiers
================================================================================

Prevailing conditions affect the difficulty of Vehicle Operation skill checks:

| Condition | Modifier |
|---|---|
| Clear | None |
| Normal | None (Routine maneuvers only) |
| Crowded | +1 penalty |
| Hazardous | +2 penalty |

Speed modifiers:
- Exceeding cruising speed: +1 penalty
- At or near maximum speed: +3 penalty

Maneuver difficulty:
- Moderate maneuver (inherent): +1 penalty
- Extreme maneuver (inherent): +3 penalty

================================================================================
  #166 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 201
  Overshooting the Target
================================================================================

If a closing vehicle's speed is so great that it would move past the target vehicle in a single phase, the closing vehicle overshoots. The closing vehicle passes the target and ends up on the other side, with the excess distance as the new range. The driver or pilot can attempt a Moderate maneuver to avoid overshooting if he wishes to end up at the target's location instead.

================================================================================
  #171 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 205
  Ramming a Character with a Vehicle
================================================================================

Running over a pedestrian who's trying to get out of the way isn't always easy -- the victim adds his Dexterity-based resistance modifier to the driver's Vehicle Operation check when the driver actually tries to execute the ram, and he can also attempt an Acrobatics-dodge skill check. If the pedestrian can't get out of the way, he suffers damage based on the speed of the vehicle that hits him. The victim must make a Dexterity feat check (or Acrobatics-fall skill check) and refer to Table P43: Crash and Collision Damage.

This feat check or skill check is modified by the type of vehicle that strikes him:

| Vehicle | Modifier |
|---|---|
| Motorcycle | -2 |
| Compact car | -1 |
| Mid-sized car | None |
| Large car, van | +1 |
| Truck or tank | +2 |

================================================================================
  #176 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 209
  Sensors Operator Actions
================================================================================

**Assist weapons operator:** System Operation-sensors check provides modifier to weapons operator's next phase: Critical Failure, +2 penalty; Failure, no modifier; Ordinary, -1 bonus; Good, -2 bonus; Amazing, -3 bonus.

**Target specific compartment:** Critical Failure, weapon misses; Failure, random determination as usual (roll d20); Ordinary, adjust random determination by +1 or -1; Good, adjust by +2 or -2; Amazing, adjust by +3 or -3.

**Assist defenses operator:** Provides modifier for rest of round and all of next round: Critical Failure, +2 penalty; Failure, no modifier; Ordinary, -1 bonus; Good, -2 bonus; Amazing, -3 bonus.

================================================================================
  #177 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 209
  Communications Encoding/Decoding
================================================================================

**Encoding transmissions** (provides penalty to decoding attempts): Critical Failure, -2 bonus (helps enemy); Failure, none; Ordinary, +1 penalty; Good, +2; Amazing, +3.

**Decoding enemy messages** (complex skill check, modified by code complexity): Marginal code, -1 bonus; Ordinary code, none; Good code, +1 penalty; Amazing code, +2 penalty.

**Jamming weapons/targeting systems:** Critical Failure, -2 bonus (helps enemy); Failure, none; Ordinary, +1 penalty; Good, +2; Amazing, +3.

================================================================================
  #180 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 211
  Spaceship Engines Explained
================================================================================

Spaceship engines come in several varieties across the Progress Levels:

- **PL 6 Ion Engine:** Powered by fusion generators or mass reactors. These engines provide thrust by accelerating ions to high velocities. Standard propulsion for PL 6 spacecraft.
- **PL 6 Planetary Thruster:** Used for atmospheric operations and achieving orbital velocity. Powers STG shuttles.
- **PL 7 Induction Engine:** Powered by mass reactors. Uses gravity induction technology for more efficient thrust. Standard for PL 7 spacecraft.
- **PL 7 Grav-Fusion Cell:** An advanced power plant combining gravity induction with fusion technology.
- **PL 8 Anomaly Inducer:** Uses controlled gravitational anomalies for propulsion. Standard for PL 8 spacecraft.
- **PL 8 Matter Converter:** The ultimate power plant, converting matter directly to energy.

**Stardrive:** Required for interstellar travel. A stardrive transitions a vessel into "drivespace," allowing faster-than-light travel. Drivespace rating indicates how many light-years per "starfall" the ship can traverse.

| d8 Roll | Result |
|---|---|
| 1-4 | Belongs to mutant community |

Mutation points are determined by rolling d4 plus a constant based on origin. Drawback points are determined by rolling d4.

================================================================================
  #184 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 217
  Penalty Reductions (Mutations)
================================================================================

Several mutations reduce the penalties a character normally suffers in adverse conditions. When a mutation provides a "step reduction" to a penalty, this means the penalty is decreased by the indicated number of steps on the situation die scale. For example, if a character would normally suffer a +2 penalty, and his mutation reduces penalties by 2 steps, the penalty is eliminated entirely.

================================================================================
  #185 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 219
  Psi Sensitivity Distance Modifiers
================================================================================

A mutant with the Psi Sensitivity mutation may detect psionic energy use. The situation die for the Awareness-intuition check is modified by distance:

| Distance (meters) | Situation Die Modifier |
|---|---|
| 0-2 | -3 |
| 3-6 | -2 |
| 7-10 | -1 |
| 11-14 | none |
| 15-18 | +1 |
| 19-22 | +2 |
| 23-25 | +3 |
| 25+ | can't sense psionics |

================================================================================
  #187 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 223
  Poison Attack Types
================================================================================

| Poison Type | Delivery System |
|---|---|
| Hemotoxin | Insinuative |
| Neurotoxin | Insinuative or inhaled |
| Irritant | Inhaled |

**Hemotoxin effects** (5 rounds after introduction): Constitution feat check by target: Critical Failure, d4+2m; Failure, d4m; Ordinary, d6+1w; Good, d4w; Amazing, d6s.

**Neurotoxin effects** (1 round after introduction): Constitution feat check by target: Critical Failure, d6+1m; Failure, d4+1m; Ordinary, d8+1w; Good, d6+1w; Amazing, d6+1s.

**Irritant effects** (next phase after introduction): Constitution feat check by target: Critical Failure, +3 penalty to all actions for 2 rounds; Failure, +2 penalty for 2 rounds; Ordinary, +1 penalty for 2 rounds; Good or Amazing, no effect.

**Biokineticist:** Biokinesis-heal 2, rejuvenate, transfer damage 2; Medical Science-treatment. Cost: 35 points.

**Biowarrior:** Biokinesis-bioweapon 2, control metabolism, rejuvenate; Melee Weapons-bludgeon. Cost: 30 points.

**ESPion:** ESP-clairvoyance 2, empathy 2, mind reading, precognition, psychometry 2; Knowledge-deduce. Cost: 35 points.

**Mystic:** ESP-clairaudience, clairvoyance, postcognition 2, precognition 2. Cost: 25 points.

**Telekineticist:** Telekinesis-kinetic shield 2, levitation, psychokinetics, pyrokinetics; Modern Ranged Weapons-pistol. Cost: 35 points.

**Psiguard:** Telekinesis-electrokinetics 2, photokinetics 2, levitation; Modern Ranged Weapons-pistol; Security-protection protocols. Cost: 40 points.

**Telepath:** Telepathy-contact 2, illusion, suggest 2; ESP-mind reading. Cost: 30 points.

**Mind Knight:** Telepathy-contact 2, mind blast 2, mind shield 2; Telekinesis-psychokinetics. Cost: 35 points.

================================================================================
  #203 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 244-245
  Cykosis
================================================================================

Cykosis is a condition that affects characters who overuse certain cybernetic enhancements, particularly the fast chip. Characters who use a fast chip regularly risk developing cykosis, a degenerative condition that manifests as erratic behavior, paranoia, violent outbursts, and eventual psychosis.

The Gamemaster tracks cykosis privately. Each time a character uses a fast chip, there is a chance of cykosis developing or worsening. The condition is measured on a scale, and at higher levels, the character's behavior becomes increasingly unpredictable and dangerous.

================================================================================
  #204 | SIDEBAR | PHB Page 246
  Enhance Programs (Reflex)
================================================================================

Enhance programs utilize reflex wiring to allow the body to perform faster, more accurately, and with better control. A character must have both a nanocomputer and reflex cybernetic circuitry installed to use enhance programs.

For every round or portion thereof that a character activates his reflex circuitry, that character suffers stun damage based on the quality of the enhance program: Ordinary, 1 point; Good, 2 points; Amazing, 3 points. On a Critical Failure, the Gamemaster may also call for a cykosis check.

| Failure | No change |
| Ordinary | Shift up 1 step |
| Good | Shift up 2 steps |
| Amazing | Shift up 3 steps |

- Combative target: Business (INT), Law (INT)
- Hostile target: Administration (WIL), Street Smart (WIL), Culture (PER)

================================================================================
  #211 | TABLE | PHB Page 249
  Compiled Table: Damage Summary
================================================================================

**Stun Damage:** Light damage; bumps, bruises, and mild abrasions.
- Dazed (optional): Damage amounting to more than half of total stun points results in a +1 penalty to all actions.
- Knockout: If all stun boxes are marked off, character is unconscious.
- Heavy Stun: Additional stun damage after all stun boxes are marked off becomes wound damage. Every 2 points of stun damage become 1 point of wound damage.

**Wound Damage:** Injuries that cause lasting harm to the body.
- Secondary Damage: For every 2 wound points suffered, also mark off 1 stun. (Armor does not absorb secondary damage.)
- Dazed (optional): Damage amounting to more than half of total wound points results in a +1 penalty to all actions.
- Knockout: If all wound boxes are marked off, character is unconscious.
- Heavy Wound: Additional wound damage after all wound boxes are marked off becomes mortal damage. Every 2 points of wound damage becomes 1 point of mortal damage.

**Mortal Damage:** Severe trauma and deadly damage.
- Secondary Damage: For every 2 mortal points suffered, also mark off 1 wound and 1 stun. (Armor does not absorb secondary damage.)
- Dazed: Each point of mortal damage results in a cumulative +1 penalty to all actions.
- Dying and Death: At the end of any scene in which mortal damage is suffered, make a Stamina-endurance check: Critical Failure, suffer 2 additional points of mortal damage; Failure, suffer 1 additional point of mortal damage; any success, no change. Check again hourly, or daily if helped through Knowledge-first aid or Medical Science-treatment. If all mortal boxes are marked off, a character dies.

**Fatigue Damage:** Exhaustion.
- Dazed: Each point of fatigue damage results in a cumulative +1 penalty to all actions.
- Knockout: When all fatigue boxes are marked, make a Resolve-physical resolve check to avoid falling unconscious.

**Amazing Damage:** If a character suffers damage as the result of an opponent's Amazing success during combat, the character makes a Stamina-endurance check as soon as the damage is applied. Failure results in knockout.

================================================================================
  #218 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 12
  Eyeballing Difficulty
================================================================================

(From the Fast-Play Rules chapter.) The Eyeballing It method for assigning situation dice:

| Modifier | Situation Die |
|---|---|
| (Easy/bonus) | -d4 to -d20 |
| (Average) | +d0 |
| (Hard/penalty) | +d4 to +d20 |

The GM simply selects the modifier that matches how difficult or easy the task should be, without tallying individual step modifiers.

  #220 | TABLE | GMG Page 21
  Ability Score Scale
================================================================================

| Ability Score | Odds (2d6+2) | You're in the Top |
|---|---|---|
| 4 | 1 in 36 (3%) | 100% |
| 5 | 2 in 36 (6%) | 97% |
| 6 | 3 in 36 (8%) | 92% |

| 8 | 5 in 36 (14%) | 72% |
| 9 | 6 in 36 (16%) | 58% |
| 10 | 5 in 36 (14%) | 42% |
| 11 | 4 in 36 (11%) | 28% |
| 12 | 3 in 36 (8%) | 17% |
| 13 | 2 in 36 (6%) | 8% |
| 14 | 1 in 36 (3%) | 3% |

Odds refer to the chance of rolling that exact Ability Score using the 2d6+2 method. "You're in the Top" describes where a hero's score fits in the general demographics of the game universe.

================================================================================
  #225 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 27
  Alien Species Design Checklist
================================================================================

10-step process for designing new alien hero species:

1. **Concept** -- General idea before game particulars
2. **Form and Physiology** -- Anatomical makeup, diet, communication
3. **History** -- Past events, inter/intra-species relationships, planet of origin
4. **Culture** -- Social institutions, government, customs, taboos, art
5. **Psychology** -- Worldview, mindset, perceptual processing
6. **Playability** -- Can it interact with environment and other heroes?
7. **Ability Score Requirements** -- Minimums/maximums (human range 4-14; aliens may go 2-16)
8. **Innate Skills** -- Free broad skills describing natural talents
9. **Advantages** -- Special abilities (action check bonus, armor, flight, natural weapons, etc.)
10. **Weaknesses** -- Balancing disadvantages (low ability scores, reduced senses, skill penalties, etc.)

================================================================================
  #226 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 29
  Example Alien Advantages
================================================================================

- Action check bonus (t'sa)
- All-around vision
- Armor (t'sa)
- Camouflage (weren)
- Environmental capability (tolerates Class 2 or 3 environments without aid)
- Flight (sesheyan)
- Mental powers (fraal)
- Natural resistance to temperature extremes, radiation, energy forms, poison, or disease
- Natural weaponry (weren)
- Poison
- Regeneration
- Increased resistance modifier to one Ability Score
- Skill bonus (mechalus, t'sa)
- Sprinting/pouncing
- Swimming/water breathing
- Toughness (weren)
- Unusual sense (sesheyan)

================================================================================
  #227 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 29
  Example Alien Weaknesses
================================================================================

- Low Ability Scores
- Suffers increased damage from low impact, high impact, or energy attacks
- Reduced senses (sesheyan)
- Action check penalty
- Skill penalty
- Automatic flaw (weren)
- Can't use certain types of equipment (armor, etc.) due to body form, cultural taboo, or other reason

================================================================================
  #228 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 31
  Flaws That Aren't Flaws
================================================================================

Some flaws have more immediate game impact than others. A Powerful Enemy may not bother a hero for months, but Fragile could crop up in any combat scene. GMs must record player flaws and USE them. If a hero's Powerful Enemy never makes an appearance, the flaw just represents free skill points. Finding the right use for a flaw in an adventure heightens dramatic tension.

================================================================================
  #231 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 32
  Weapon and Armor Availability
================================================================================

Grenades and heavy weapons shouldn't be freely available to all heroes everywhere. Many weapons and top armor are illegal in civilized locales. Sidearms may be reasonable in rough regions, but rifles, heavy weapons, and explosives aren't acceptable in many places. Heroes stepping off their ship into a starport, city, or space station should leave plasma guns and mass rifles behind. Progress Level determines what technology is available.

================================================================================
  #232 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 32
  What Every Hero Owns
================================================================================

Even if a hero buys nothing else, it's assumed he begins play with: two or three changes of street clothes, shoes, a wallet, a cheap wristwatch, basic jewelry, a toiletry kit, and maybe a suitcase, bag, or trunk to carry it all in.
