================================================================================
  #234 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 36
  Resistance Modifiers by Skill
================================================================================

The following skills use the listed Ability Score for their resistance modifier:

| Skill | Resistance Modifier Based On |
|---|---|
| Melee Weapons | Strength |
| Unarmed Attack | Strength |
| Modern Ranged Weapons | Dexterity |
| Primitive Ranged Weapons | Dexterity |
| Stealth | Intelligence or Will |
| Street Smart | Intelligence or Will |
| Psionic Skills | Intelligence or Will |

================================================================================
  #235 | TABLE | GMG Page 36
  Degrees of Success
================================================================================

| Result | Condition |
|---|---|
| Critical Failure | 20 on control die |
| Failure/Marginal | Higher than skill score |
| Ordinary | Equal to or less than skill score |
| Good | Equal to or less than half skill score |
| Amazing | Equal to or less than quarter skill score |
| Automatic Success | 1 on control die |

================================================================================
  #236 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 37
  Make the Results Memorable
================================================================================

Tips on using complex skill checks for suspense and tension. Characters can accumulate successes over time. Competitive character actions can also use simultaneous complex skill checks to build drama.

================================================================================
  #237 | TABLE | GMG Page 40
  G7: Detection Modifiers
================================================================================

**Size:**

| Size | Modifier |
|---|---|
| Tiny | +3 penalty |
| Small | +1 penalty |
| Average | none |
| Large | -1 bonus |
| Huge | -3 bonus |

**Range:**

| Range | Modifier |
|---|---|
| Far | +3 penalty |
| Medium | +1 penalty |
| Close | none |
| Very close | -1 bonus |

**Background/Camouflage:**

| Condition | Modifier |
|---|---|
| Camouflaged | +3 penalty |
| Obscured | +1 penalty |
| Indistinct | none |
| Contrast | -1 bonus |
| Clashing | -3 bonus |

**Light:**

| Condition | Modifier |
|---|---|
| Total darkness | +3 penalty |
| Moonlight | +1 penalty |
| Twilight | none |
| Daylight | -1 bonus |
| Bright sun | -3 bonus |

Choose a condition from each column and add the modifiers together to produce the total modifier.

================================================================================
  #238 | TABLE | GMG Page 40
  G8: Visual Detection Ranges
================================================================================

| Visibility | Person | Vehicle | Terrain Feature |
|---|---|---|---|
| Amazing (full sun) | 2000 m | 10000 m | 100 km |
| Good (bright room) | 1000 m | 5000 m | 50 km |
| Ordinary (average) | 500 m | 2500 m | 25 km |
| Marginal (cloudy) | 100 m | 500 m | 5 km |
| Slight (twilight/rain) | 50 m | 100 m | 2 km |
| Moderate (moonlight/fog) | 20 m | 50 m | 500 m |
| Extreme (total darkness) | 2 m | 5 m | 10 m |

================================================================================
  #239 | TABLE | GMG Page 41
  G9: Exhaustion (Overland March)
================================================================================

When marching overland, the speed of the march determines how often a hero must make a Stamina-endurance skill check to avoid fatigue damage.

| Result | Fatigue Damage |
|---|---|
| Critical Failure | 2 points |
| Failure | 1 point |
| Any success | no damage |

For characters with the Movement broad skill, the frequency of Stamina-endurance checks is reduced by 1 hour per category. Penalties caused by each point of fatigue damage apply to subsequent Stamina-endurance checks.

**Terrain Modifiers:**
- Smooth terrain (plains, scrubland, trails): No penalty
- Varied terrain (sand, hills, light forest): +2 penalty
- Rugged terrain (jungle, swamp, deep snow, mountains): +3 penalty
- Darkness, inclement weather, icy/slippery terrain: additional +1 penalty each

================================================================================
  #240 | TABLE | GMG Page 42
  G10: Mounted Travel
================================================================================

| Mount Quality | Stroll (km/hr) | March (km/hr) | Forced March (km/hr) |
|---|---|---|---|
| Marginal (CON 10) | 6 | 8 | -- |
| Ordinary (CON 12) | 6 | 10 | -- |
| Good (CON 14) | 8 | 12 | -- |
| Amazing (CON 16) | 10 | 14 | -- |

- **Stroll:** The hero rides at a walking pace, dismounting to lead frequently.
- **March:** The hero rides at a walking pace but may trot or canter for short periods. Dismounts and leads occasionally.
- **Forced March:** The hero presses his mount hard, taking long canters and dismounting only when the animal is desperate for rest.

================================================================================
  #241 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 43-44
  Surprise Modifiers
================================================================================

Factors that may affect a surprise check (Awareness skill check):
- Quality of the ambush (Stealth-hide degree of success: Ordinary +1, Good +2, Amazing +3 penalty to targets)
- Cover available (light +1, medium +2, heavy +3 penalty to targets)
- Terrain adjustment for groups in motion
- Distraction, noise, or other environmental factors at GM discretion

================================================================================
  #242 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 45
  Overpower Summary
================================================================================

Overpower attack: normal attack with +1 penalty (plus resistance modifier). Each ally joining in same phase provides -1 bonus. Successful overpower establishes a hold equal to degree of success (Ordinary +1, Good +2, Amazing +3 penalty to held character).

Options after establishing hold:
- **Improve the Hold:** Better attack = increased penalty; failed attack loses hold
- **Bum's Rush:** Drag/push held character
- **Maul:** Normal unarmed damage; failed attack loses hold
- **Takedown:** Put held character on ground (prone penalties +2)
- **Pin:** Third consecutive overpower attack; pinned character can't get free

Breaking free: Unarmed Attack or Acrobatics check, or Strength/Dexterity feat check. Amazing success = immediate action in same phase.

================================================================================
  #243 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 47
  Friendly Fire
================================================================================

When using autofire against multiple targets within 6 meters of each other, the attacker bases the situation die on the most difficult target. If allies are in the area of fire, there is a risk of hitting them. Area-effect weapons always endanger friendly characters within the blast radius.

================================================================================
  #244 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 47
  Autofire Rules Summary
================================================================================

Using autofire: hero makes three attacks using one control die and three situation dice.
- 1st shot: +1 penalty from base
- 2nd shot: +2 penalty from base
- 3rd shot: +3 penalty from base

May strike three different targets (must be within 6 meters of each other) or hammer one opponent up to three times. Each hit treated separately for damage. When targeting multiple enemies, compute situation die based on the most difficult target.

================================================================================
  #245 | TABLE | GMG Page 48
  P20: Accuracy by Range (Area-Effect Weapons)
================================================================================

| Result | Short | Medium | Long |
|---|---|---|---|
| Failure | -- | -- | 12 m miss |
| Ordinary | on target | 2 m miss* | 4 m miss |
| Good | on target | on target | 2 m miss |
| Amazing | always on target | always on target | always on target |

*For thrown objects or indirect fire weapons.

Scatter is determined randomly when a miss occurs.

================================================================================
  #246 | TABLE | GMG Page 49-50
  G11: Terrain in Combat
================================================================================

| Terrain | Movement Rate | Examples |
|---|---|---|
| Smooth | normal | firm sand, earth, light brush |
| Varied | 1/2 normal | knee-deep water, loose sand, jungle, moving uphill |
| Rugged | 1/4 normal | waist-deep water, deep snow or mud, thick jungle, steep slope |

================================================================================
  #247 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 49-50
  Supporting Cast Action Checks & Teamwork
================================================================================

Guidelines for handling action checks and teamwork for supporting cast members. Simplify by rolling a single action check for groups of similar NPCs. Allow supporting cast members to assist each other just as heroes do. Don't insult villain intelligence by forcing them to always work alone while heroes cooperate.

================================================================================
  #248 | TABLE | GMG Page 50-51
  G12: Visibility in Combat
================================================================================

| Condition | Modifier |
|---|---|
| Starlight, dark building | +1 penalty |
| Total darkness, underground | +3 penalty (or more) |

(Additional visibility penalties are applied at GM discretion based on conditions like moonlight, twilight, etc.)

================================================================================
  #249 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 51
  Sneak Attack Bonuses
================================================================================

Hero's Stealth skill check determines bonus to first attack:
- Ordinary success: -1 bonus
- Good success: -2 bonus
- Amazing success: -3 bonus

Can execute sneak attack with melee weapon, unarmed attack, or ranged attack. Requires available cover/obscurity, or approach from the rear.

================================================================================
  #250 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 51
  Suppressive Fire
================================================================================

Character makes normal skill check but instead of inflicting damage, the result imposes a penalty to target's ranged attacks during the phase:
- Ordinary: +1 penalty to target
- Good: +2 penalty to target
- Amazing: +3 penalty to target

Autofire suppressive fire can affect up to three enemies. Effects not cumulative (only best result applies). Targets who ignore suppressive fire instead take normal damage for the indicated hit.

================================================================================
  #251 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 51
  Called Shot Options
================================================================================

Called shot adds +4 penalty. Cannot use burst or autofire. Options:
- **Disarm:** Strike weapon from opponent's hand; no damage
- **Dead-Eye Shot:** Degree of success increases by one grade (Ordinary->Good, Good->Amazing)
- **Equipment Damage:** Damage something another character holds/carries
- **Style Shot:** Inflicts no damage except humiliation (singe clothing, cut hair, etc.)
- **Trick Shot:** Outlandish feat of marksmanship; penalty may increase to +6 or more

================================================================================
  #252 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 51-52
  Threaten
================================================================================

Character makes skill check but instead of inflicting damage, threatens the target. In any subsequent phase or round, can automatically strike before the threatened target (regardless of action check). Damage determined by initial skill check. Must be within striking/maximum range. Threat broken if threatening character does anything else. Most enemies won't ignore being threatened (Will feat check may be required).

================================================================================
  #253 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 51
  Charge (Combat Tactic)
================================================================================

A charging hero ignores penalties associated with attacking while running and gains a -2 bonus to his skill check. Downside: opponents gain a -2 bonus to strike the charging hero. Once engaged in melee, can't charge again until free and clear.

================================================================================
  #254 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 52
  Two Weapons
================================================================================

Hero makes two separate skill checks. Penalties: +2 with primary hand, +4 with secondary hand. If Ambidextrous: primary hand penalty negated, secondary hand drops to +2. Good tactic: attack with primary weapon, reserve secondary for parries.

================================================================================
  #255 | TABLE | GMG Page 53-54
  Firepower and Toughness
================================================================================

**Firepower Ratings:**
- Ordinary: Most personal weapons
- Good: Many heavy weapons, plasma guns
- Amazing: Large vehicular weapons, spaceship weapons

**Toughness Ratings:**
- Ordinary: Humanoid species, most personal armor, portable objects
- Good: Vehicles, buildings, some personal armor (powered attack armor, body tanks)
- Amazing: Tanks, fortified buildings, spaceships

**Damage Degradation:**
- Ordinary firepower vs. Good toughness: mortal -> wound, wound -> stun, stun -> ignored
- Ordinary firepower vs. Amazing toughness: mortal -> stun, wound -> ignored, stun -> ignored
- Good firepower vs. Amazing toughness: mortal -> wound, wound -> stun, stun -> ignored
- If firepower >= toughness: no degradation

================================================================================
  #256 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 54
  Stun Recovery
================================================================================

Stun damage automatically disappears at the end of a scene. Medical Science-treatment or Knowledge-first aid can remove stun damage during a scene and restore consciousness. An unconscious hero who doesn't receive medical attention remains unconscious for the rest of the round and all of the next round. Thereafter, he can attempt a Resolve-physical resolve check every round: Ordinary = 2 stun points recovered; Good = 4 stun points; Amazing = 6 stun points. No actions in the round of recovery.

================================================================================
  #257 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 55
  Wound Recovery
================================================================================

Wounds don't disappear at end of scene. Without medical treatment, each week the hero may make a Resolve-physical resolve check:

| Result | Wounds Recovered |
|---|---|
| Critical Failure | Condition worsens, +1 wound |
| Marginal | 1 wound |
| Ordinary | 2 wounds |
| Good | 3 wounds |
| Amazing | 4 wounds |

Complete rest for the week: -2 bonus. Normal activity: +2 penalty. If unconscious (all wound points lost), can't regain consciousness until at least 1 wound healed.

================================================================================
  #258 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 55
  Mortal Damage and Dying
================================================================================

Each point of mortal damage causes a +1 penalty to all actions. A character with any mortal damage is dying. At end of scene: Stamina-endurance check -- Critical Failure = 2 additional mortal; Failure = 1 additional mortal; any success = no additional mortal. Thereafter, dying character must check every hour. If all mortal boxes marked off, character dies. Mortal damage can only be healed by medical skills (Knowledge-first aid stabilizes; Medical Science-surgery heals).

================================================================================
  #259 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 56
  Death and Resurrection
================================================================================

No standard game mechanic for restoring life to the dead. In high-tech campaigns, medical technologies may revive a dead character, but this should NOT be routine. Limits: finest medical facilities only; time of the essence (1-2 hours max); unusual circumstances (cold-water drowning, freezing, alien toxins) may allow return to life. The hero or comrades should pay a price for a second chance -- a great plot device. Don't treat a brush with death as mundane.

================================================================================
  #260 | TABLE | GMG Page 57
  G13: Object Armor
================================================================================

| Armor Type | Damage Stopped |
|---|---|
| Fragile | none |
| Light | d4 |
| Moderate | d6+2 |
| Heavy | 2d4+1 |

| Failure | 2d4w* |
| Ordinary | d4w |
| Good | no damage |
| Amazing | no damage |

*Damage continues each round, diminishing by one die per round. If character neutralizes the acid immediately, damage ceases.

================================================================================
  #262 | TABLE | GMG Page 58
  Disease Resistance
================================================================================

**Initial Constitution Feat Check:**

| Check Result | Effect |
|---|---|
| Critical Failure | Terminally ill |
| Failure | Extremely ill |
| Ordinary | Ill |
| Good | No effect |
| Amazing | No effect |

**Disease Strength Modifiers:**

| Strength | Modifier |
|---|---|
| Marginal | -1 bonus |
| Ordinary | no modifier |
| Good | +1 penalty |
| Amazing | +3 penalty |

**Incubation Periods:**

| Incubation | Onset |
|---|---|
| Marginal | 1d4 weeks |
| Ordinary | 2d4 days |
| Good | 1d4 days |
| Amazing | 3d4 hours |

================================================================================
  #263 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 58-59
  Disease Effects
================================================================================

**Ill:** +2 penalty to all actions. Each day, Constitution feat check: Critical Failure/Failure = worsen to extremely ill; Ordinary = no change; Good/Amazing = recover.

**Extremely Ill:** Almost completely incapacitated. May attempt Resolve-physical resolve check to force himself to feet, but all actions receive +3 penalty. Each day, Constitution feat check: Critical Failure/Failure = worsen to terminally ill; Ordinary = no change; Good = improve to ill; Amazing = recover completely.

**Terminally Ill:** Comatose (can rouse for a few words with Resolve check). Every six hours, Constitution feat check: Critical Failure = 2 mortal damage; Failure = 1 mortal damage; Ordinary = no change; Good/Amazing = improve to extremely ill.

================================================================================
  #264 | TABLE | GMG Page 59
  G15: Electrical Damage
================================================================================

| CON Feat Check Result | Shock Damage |
|---|---|
| Critical Failure | d12w |
| Failure | d8w |
| Ordinary | d6s |
| Good | d4s |
| Amazing | no damage |

Modifiers: dripping wet on iron grate +3 penalty; well-insulated with rubber gloves -3 bonus.

================================================================================
  #265 | TABLE | GMG Page 59
  Fall Categories and Time
================================================================================

**Fall Categories:**
- Extremely Short: 3 meters or less
- Short: 3 to 10 meters
- Medium: 11 to 30 meters
- Long: 31 to 60 meters
- Terminal: 61+ meters

**Time Falling:**

| Length of Fall | Time Falling |
|---|---|
| Up to 60 meters | 1 phase |
| 60-200 meters | 2 phases |
| 200-400 meters | 3 phases |
| 400-600 meters | 4 phases |
| +200 meters | add 1 phase |

================================================================================
  #266 | TABLE | GMG Page 59

|---|---|---|---|---|---|

| Failure | d4+2w | d4+2m | d8+2m | d12+6m | -- |
| Ordinary | d4+1w | d4+1m | d6+2m | d8+6m | -- |

================================================================================
  #267 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 59
  Fall Modifiers
================================================================================

Modifiers to the hero's roll on Table P15: Impact Damage:
- Landing on soft surface (water, deep snow, soft earth): may reduce fall category by one grade
- Landing on hard/spiked surface: may increase fall category
- Low gravity: reduce fall category (see Table G18)
- High gravity: increase fall category (see Table G18)
- Armor can't counter fall damage, but may negate extra damage from spikes or devices

================================================================================
  #268 | TABLE | GMG Page 60
  G16: Fire Damage
================================================================================

| CON Feat Check Result | Heat/Smoke | Flame |
|---|---|---|
| Critical Failure | 2d6s* | 3d6w |
| Failure | 2d6s | 2d6w |
| Ordinary | d6s | d6w |
| Good | d4s | d6s |
| Amazing | no damage | no damage** |

*Treat as "on fire" in following rounds.
**If a character or object has caught fire, this result indicates the fire is extinguished.

Modifiers: Respirator or independent oxygen supply upgrades success by one step. Heat-reflective or insulated clothing upgrades by another step. Character can use armor's Energy (En) rating to negate some damage.

================================================================================
  #269 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 60
  Catching Fire
================================================================================

A hero can spend an action dropping to the ground, wrapping himself in a blanket, or taking similar protective measures to extinguish fire. In this case, any successful result on the Constitution feat check indicates the fire is extinguished. Secondary hazards from major fires include burning wreckage, structural collapse, exploding volatiles, and electrical shorts.

================================================================================
  #270 | TABLE | GMG Page 61
  G17: Poison Damage
================================================================================

| CON Feat Check Result | Hemotoxin | Necrotoxin | Neurotoxin | Caustic Agent | Paralytic | Irritant |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Critical Failure | d4+2m | d6+1m | d4+1m | d4m | d4 days paralyzed | d4 hours |
| Failure | d4m | d4+1m | 1d4w | d8+1w | +3 penalty | +3 penalty |
| Ordinary | d8+1w | d8+1w | 2d4w | d6w | +2 penalty | +2 penalty |
| Good | d4w | d8+1s | d4w | d4w | +1 penalty | +1 penalty |
| Amazing | d6s | -- | none | d4s | no effect | no effect |

At the end of onset time, the victim suffers the listed damage or the listed penalty to all actions, or is paralyzed for the listed duration.

================================================================================
  #271 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 61
  Six Common Poisons
================================================================================

(Referenced but the specific list of six common poisons appears nearby in the text. Poison types include hemotoxins, neurotoxins, necrotoxins, caustic agents, paralytic venoms, and irritants. Each has characteristic onset times and durations.)

**Average Onset Times and Durations:**
- Hemotoxin: onset 10 minutes, duration 4 hours
- Neurotoxin: onset 1 minute, duration 10 minutes
- Necrotoxin: onset 1 hour, duration 12 hours
- Caustic Agent: onset 5 minutes, duration 4 hours
- Paralytic Venom: onset 1 minute, duration depends on CON check
- Irritant: onset 1 round, duration 10 minutes after exposure ends

**Poison Vectors:** Insinuative (injected), Inhaled (gas/dust/aerosol), Contact (skin), Ingestive (consumed).

================================================================================
  #272 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 61-62
  Starvation and Thirst
================================================================================

Treat the lack of food or water as disease. Over time, victims become ill, extremely ill, and finally terminally ill. People can live on minimal food for several months, and survive several weeks with no food at all. Water is much more critical -- going a few days without water can kill. Use the disease progression rules (ill -> extremely ill -> terminally ill) to model effects.

================================================================================
  #273 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 61
  Poison Treatment
================================================================================

Medical Science-treatment check provides -1, -2, or -3 bonus to victim's Constitution feat check (which may be rerolled after medical attention). If the medic has the specific antidote, the victim may shift Constitution feat check result by two grades (e.g., Critical Failure becomes Ordinary success).

================================================================================
  #274 | TABLE | GMG Page 62
  Suffocation Damage
================================================================================

Characters can hold breath for rounds equal to half Constitution score. After that, each round make a Stamina-endurance check with cumulative +1 penalty:

| Check Result | Stun Damage |
|---|---|
| Critical Failure | 4 stuns |
| Failure | 3 stuns |
| Ordinary | 2 stuns |
| Good | 1 stun |
| Amazing | none |

Once stun points exhausted, unconsciousness usually follows. Damage continues as wounds instead of stuns.

================================================================================
  #275 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 62
  The Endurance Challenge
================================================================================

Two types of endurance challenges:

**Exposure Challenge** (direct harm: heat, cold, poison atmosphere):
Stamina-endurance check determines stun damage:

| Check Result | Stun Damage |
|---|---|
| Critical Failure | 4 stun points |
| Failure | 3 stun points |
| Ordinary | 2 stun points |
| Good | 1 stun point |
| Amazing | no damage |

Interval depends on severity (once per phase to once per hour). Some impose cumulative +1 step penalty. Once stun exhausted, wound damage at same rate. Once wound exhausted, character begins dying.

**Exhaustion Challenge** (thin atmosphere, heavy gravity, heavy labor):
Stamina-endurance check determines fatigue damage:

| Check Result | Fatigue Damage |
|---|---|
| Critical Failure | 2 points |
| Failure | 1 point |
| Any success | no damage |

Once fatigue exhausted, character collapses. If he pushes on, suffers stun damage at same rate.

================================================================================
  #276 | TABLE | GMG Page 63
  GRAPH System Overview
================================================================================

The GRAPH system rates five primary environmental factors, each divided into six grades:

| Letter | Factor | Grades |
|---|---|---|
| G | Gravity | G0 (Zero) through G5 (Super High) |
| R | Radiation | R0 (Zero) through R5 (Lethal) |
| A | Atmospheric Composition | A0 (Vacuum) through A5 (Super Corrosive) |
| P | Pressure | P0 (Vacuum) through P5 (Crushing) |
| H | Heat/Cold | H0 (Absolute Zero) through H5 (Inferno) |

Example: Earth = G2/R1/A2/P3/H2

================================================================================
  #277 | TABLE | GMG Page 64

================================================================================

| Gravity Grade | Physical Penalty | Movement Modifier | Fall Modifier | Exhaustion Check |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| G0 (Zero) | +3 | special | no falls | -- |
| G1 (Low, 0.2-0.8g) | +1 | +50% | -1 grade | -- |
| G2 (Moderate, 0.8-1.2g) | none | none | none | -- |
| G3 (High, 1.2-2.0g) | +1 | -25% | +1 grade | 1/day |
| G4 (Very High, 2.0-4.0g) | +3 | -75% | +3 grades | 1/hour |
| G5 (Super High, 4.0g+) | +5 | -100% | +4 grades | 1/minute |

|---|---|---|

| R4 (Extreme, <500 rems/hr) | +1 penalty | 1/hour |
| R5 (Lethal, 500+ rems/hr) | +3 penalty | 1/minute |

================================================================================
  #280 | TABLE | GMG Page 65-66

================================================================================

| Grade | Description | Effect | Protection |
|---|---|---|---|
| A0 | Vacuum | See P0: Vacuum | -- |
| A1 | Inert (no free oxygen) | Suffocation; exposure checks 1/round cumulative +1 | Vacuum mask, e-suit |

| A3 | Toxic | Exposure checks 1/minute | Respirator mask |

  #281 | TABLE | GMG Page 65-66

================================================================================

| Grade | Pressure (atm) | Effect | Protection |
|---|---|---|---|
| P0 | Vacuum | Exposure checks 1/phase cumulative +1; suffocation + shock | Sealed respiration + skin cover |
| P1 | Very Thin (0.2-0.5) | Endurance checks 1/hour; altitude sickness | Respirator mask |
| P2 | Thin (0.5-0.8) | +2 penalty to exertion Stamina checks | Respirator mask |
| P3 | Moderate (0.8-4.0) | No danger | -- |
| P4 | Dense (4.0-20.0) | Endurance checks 1/hour (1/day with respirator) | E-suit for complete protection |
| P5 | Crushing (20.0+) | Exposure checks 1/phase | Space vehicle only |

  #282 | TABLE | GMG Page 66
  Heat and Cold Effects (GRAPH "H" Factor)
================================================================================

| Grade | Temperature | Unprotected Checks | Soft E-Suit | Hard E-Suit |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| H0 | Absolute Zero (<-200C) | 1/phase | 1/hour | Complete protection |
| H1 | Frigid (<-50C) | 1/round | 1/hour (heavy clothing) | Complete protection |
| H2 | Temperate (-50C to 50C) | None (or 1/hour in extremes) | -- | -- |
| H3 | Torrid (50C to 100C) | 1/minute | 1/10 minutes | Complete protection |
| H4 | Super Torrid (100C to 500C) | 1/phase | 1/minute | 1/10 minutes |
| H5 | Inferno (500C+) | 1/phase cumulative +1 | No protection | No protection |

================================================================================
  #283 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 69
  It's Your Game
================================================================================

Reminder that the Gamemaster has final say on all skill rulings. If a skill isn't explicitly covered, the GM should use common sense and the core mechanic to resolve the action. Players should be encouraged to find creative uses for their skills.

================================================================================
  #284 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 69
  Complex Skill Check Rules
================================================================================

**Successes by Degree:**
- Ordinary result = 1 success
- Good result = 2 successes
- Amazing result = 3 successes
- Failure = 0 successes (no progress)

**Three Strikes Rule:** If a character rolls three Failure results during a complex skill check, the attempt is ruined. The task is beyond the character's ability until conditions change.

**Critical Failure during Complex Check -- possible outcomes:**
- Disaster: harmful event triggered (files erased, alarms triggered, equipment damaged)
- Start Over: all accumulated successes erased
- Vain Effort: complex check ends in failure; can't be reattempted until conditions change

**Complexity determines successes required:**
- Marginal: least complex
- Amazing: most complex

================================================================================
  #285 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 69-70
  Overlooked Skills
================================================================================

Three categories of skills players often forget:

1. **Innate Skills:** Species defaults every character has (see Table P4).
2. **Broad Skills:** Purchasing a broad skill provides basic ability in all its specialty skills (with +d4 base situation die), except prohibited skills.
3. **Untrained Skills:** Heroes can try to use most skills at untrained scores (half Ability Score). Unless a skill is prohibited, any hero can attempt it.

Common untrained skills heroes might use: Any combat skill, Movement, Survival, Acrobatics, Manipulation, Stealth, any Intelligence-based broad skill, Investigate, Resolve, Culture, Deception, Leadership.

================================================================================
  #286 | TABLE | GMG Page 70
  G21: Breaking Objects
================================================================================

Strength feat check modifiers for breaking objects:

**Toughness Modifier:**

| Toughness | Modifier |
|---|---|
| Ordinary | none |
| Good | +3 |
| Amazing | +6 |

**Durability Modifier:**

| Durability | Modifier |
|---|---|
| Fragile | none |
| Average | +1 |
| High | +3 |

================================================================================
  #287 | TABLE | GMG Page 71
  Lifting Objects
================================================================================

A hero can lift an object weighing up to:

| Difficulty | Weight (x STR in kg) | Penalty |
|---|---|---|
| Marginal | up to 5x | none |
| Slight | up to 10x | +1 |
| Moderate | up to 15x | +2 |
| Extreme | up to 20x | +3 |

A clean and jerk or over-the-head press may suffer an additional +2 penalty.

================================================================================
  #288 | TABLE | GMG Page 71
  Climb Distances (Complex Skill Check)
================================================================================

| Distance | Successes Needed | Time Between Checks |
|---|---|---|
| 1-30 m | 2 | 1/minute |
| 30-100 m | 4 | 1/5 minutes |
| 100-1000 m | 6 | 1/30 minutes |
| 1000+ m | 10+ | 1/hour |

Long climbs are fatiguing; treat as forced marches for fatigue checks. A Failure on a climb check is not a fall (just no progress). Falls may occur on Critical Failure.

================================================================================
  #289 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 72
  When Skills and Feats Overlap
================================================================================

When a hero has overlapping skills (e.g., Athletics-jump and Acrobatics for vertical jumps), the player can choose whichever is better. Skill rank benefits from one skill (such as bonus jump distance from Athletics-jump ranks) can still apply even if the hero uses the alternate skill check.

================================================================================
  #290 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 72
  Hang Glider Descent Rate
================================================================================

Hang gliders travel ~40-60 kph. Unpowered gliders drop 1m per 10m forward. With skill check:
- Ordinary: 1m per 20m
- Good/Amazing: 1m per 50m

Ultralights reach ~100 kph, allow continuous flight and modest ascents.

================================================================================
  #291 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 72
  Skydiving Risk
================================================================================

**Normal jump:**
- Failure: damage as Extremely Short fall
- Critical Failure: damage as Short fall

**High-risk jump** (no daredevil skill, night jumps, building/cliff jumps, low-altitude <500m):
- Critical Failure: chute doesn't open (terminal velocity fall)
- Failure: damage as Short fall
- Ordinary: damage as Extremely Short fall

================================================================================
  #292 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 73
  Lockpick Tool Quality
================================================================================

| Tool Quality | Modifier |
|---|---|
| Minimal (bobby pin, wire, nail file) | no modifier |
| Good (specialized picks and hooks) | -2 bonus |
| Amazing (fiber-optic scopes, ultrasonic transducers, magnetic manipulators) | -3 bonus |

================================================================================
  #293 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 73
  Pickpocket Returns
================================================================================

Random pocket: $5 to $60 (5d12) per wallet. Takes about 10-15 minutes to set up. People eventually notice; practicing too long in one place brings irate victims. Small towns and thinly populated areas are especially dangerous.

================================================================================
  #294 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 73
  Escape/Contortion (Prestidigitation)
================================================================================

| Bond Quality | Modifier |
|---|---|
| Good bonds (well-tied ropes) | +1 penalty |
| Amazing bonds (chained straitjacket) | +3 penalty |

================================================================================
  #295 | TABLE | GMG Page 75
  G22: Buying & Selling
================================================================================

| Skill Check Result | Buying Price | Selling Price |
|---|---|---|
| Marginal | 100% + (d20 x 10%) of cost | 100% - (d4 x 10%) of cost |
| Ordinary | 100% + (d4 x 10%) of cost | 100% - (d8 x 1%) of cost |
| Good | 100% - (d8 x 1%) of cost | 100% - (d20 x 1%) of cost |
| Amazing | 100% - (d20 x 1%) of cost | 100% - (d4 x 10%) of cost |

(Note: OCR artifacts may affect some values. The buying column shows markup over base cost; selling column shows markdown. Better results yield better prices.)

================================================================================
  #296 | TABLE | GMG Page 75
  Illicit Business -- Fencing Stolen Property

| Result | Return |
|---|---|
| Critical Failure | 5% of value |
| Marginal | 10% of value |
| Ordinary | 30% of value |
| Good | 50% of value |
| Amazing | 80% of value |

Survival skill check result applies modifiers to Stamina-endurance checks in hazardous environments:

| Result | Modifier |
|---|---|
| Critical Failure | +2 penalty |
| Failure | no modifier |
| Ordinary | -1 bonus |
| Good | -2 bonus |
| Amazing | -3 bonus |

  Law Enforcement -- Avoiding Arrest
================================================================================

| Crime Severity | Modifier |
|---|---|
| Minor violation | -2 bonus |
| Misdemeanor | none |
| Nonviolent felony | +1 penalty |
| Violent felony | +3 penalty |
| Heinous felony | +5 penalty |

================================================================================
  #299 | TABLE | GMG Page 77
  Law Enforcement -- Bond Hearings
================================================================================

| Success | Bond Result |
|---|---|
| Critical Failure | Incarcerated without bond |
| Marginal | High bail ($50,000 or more) |
| Ordinary | Moderate bail ($10,000) |
| Good | Low bail ($2,000) |
| Amazing | Released on own recognizance |

================================================================================
  #300 | TABLE | GMG Page 77
  Forensics Information by Success
================================================================================

| Success Level | Information Yielded |
|---|---|
| Marginal | Victim's blood type, obvious cause of death |
| Ordinary | Indirect cause of death, identify wounds received before/after death, minor evidence about attacker (size, dress, hair color) |
| Good | Subtle or unexpected cause of death, identify murder weapon, detailed facts about attacker's appearance or dress |
| Amazing | Disguised or deliberately altered cause of death, exacting information about attacker's identity |

================================================================================
  #301 | TABLE | GMG Page 77
  Psychology Treatment Complexity
================================================================================

| Trauma Severity | Description | Treatment Frequency |
|---|---|---|
| Marginal | Mild (e.g., mild claustrophobia) | 1 check/day |
| Slight | Moderate behavioral variance | 1 check/week |
| Moderate | Significant incapacitation | 1 check/week to 1/month |
| Extreme | Ruthless psychotic or catatonic | 1 check/month to 1/year |

Severity determines number of successes required (complex skill check).

================================================================================
  #302 | TABLE | GMG Page 78-79
  Repair Complexity
================================================================================

| Damage Type | Complexity | Successes Needed | Check Frequency |
|---|---|---|---|
| Stun damage | Ordinary | 3 | 1/round |
| Wound damage (< half total) | Good | 4 | 1/minute |
| Wound damage (> half total) | Good | 4 | 1/hour |
| Mortal damage | Amazing | 8 + 1 per mortal point | 1/day |

================================================================================
  #303 | TABLE | GMG Page 78
  Security System Complexity
================================================================================

Use complex skill checks to both set and bypass security devices. The degree of success achieved by the installer determines the complexity of bypassing:

| Installer's Success | Successes Needed to Bypass |
|---|---|
| Ordinary system | 3 successes |
| Good system | 5 successes |
| Amazing system | 8 successes |

================================================================================
  #304 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 79
  Weapon Permits (Administration Skill)
================================================================================

- Common weapons: Ordinary requests
- Controlled weapons: Good requests
- Military weapons: Amazing requests

Heroes with criminal records have a harder time obtaining permits. Other Administration uses: Equipment Requisition, File Access, Logging Claims, Passports and Visas.

================================================================================
  #305 | TABLE | GMG Page 80
  Creativity-Writing Modifier
================================================================================

When substituting written communication for a live Interaction attempt:

| Creativity-Writing Check | Modifier to Interaction Skill |
|---|---|
| Critical Failure | +4 penalty |
| Failure | +2 penalty |
| Ordinary | no modifier |
| Good | -1 bonus |
| Amazing | -2 bonus |

================================================================================
  #306 | TABLE | GMG Page 80
  Street Smart Enhancement
================================================================================

Street Smart can enhance another skill (Interaction, Deception, Business, Stealth):

| Street Smart Check | Modifier to Second Skill |
|---|---|
| Critical Failure | +2 penalty |
| Failure | no modifier |
| Ordinary | -1 bonus |
| Good | -2 bonus |
| Amazing | -3 bonus |

================================================================================
  #307 | TABLE | GMG Page 81
  Bribe Guidelines
================================================================================

| Amount | Situation |
|---|---|
| $100 | Low risk, minor infraction |
| $500 | Low risk, ordinary infraction |
| $2,000 | High risk, serious infraction |
| $10,000 | Grave risk, deadly infraction |

Risk = risk to the person receiving the bribe. Infraction = what the hero is asking the recipient to do or allow. High-profile individuals tend to require hefty bribes.

================================================================================
  #308 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 81
  Personality Skills vs. Heroes
================================================================================

Guidelines for when Personality-based encounter skills (Interaction, Deception, Leadership) are used against heroes. Players should generally be allowed to decide how their heroes react to social manipulation, but the GM can call for Resolve checks when appropriate. The Will resistance modifier applies to most social skill attempts. Attitude modifiers from Table P25: Encounter Skill Effects affect difficulty.

================================================================================
  #309 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 84
  Acquiring New Perks / Getting Rid of Flaws
================================================================================

- A hero may purchase a new perk as an achievement benefit at high enough level, but the limit of three perks still applies.
- On rare occasions, GM may assign a new perk to reward exceptional roleplaying or reflect campaign developments (e.g., earning a Reputation or becoming a Celebrity).
- Buying off a flaw is an available achievement benefit. The hero retains any bonus skill points received during character generation.
- GM may also strike a flaw if it isn't being roleplayed properly, but should withhold achievement points to compensate.

================================================================================
  #310 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 85
  Perk and Flaw Mechanics
================================================================================

**Active Perks:** Don't require skill or feat checks; provide a permanent modifier or benefit (e.g., Ambidextrous, Heightened Ability).

**Conscious Perks:** Only come into play when the hero makes a determined attempt. Require a perk check (feat check with +d4 base situation die using the hero's appropriate Ability Score). GM can assign modifiers for appropriate or inappropriate situations.

**All Flaws are Active:** Some have no effect until triggered (e.g., Phobia only activates when confronted by the feared thing).

================================================================================
  #311 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 90
  The Nonprofessional
================================================================================

Of the characters who populate a typical campaign setting, 60 to 80 percent are nonprofessionals. These are everyday folks (teacher, laborer, etc.) who aren't quite as capable as beginning heroes but may have substantial skill from profession lists. Not every person in a military uniform is a Combat Spec -- many low-ranking soldiers and junior officers don't have any profession at all.

================================================================================
  #312 | TABLE | GMG Page 90 (continuing from page 93)
  Nonprofessional Supporting Character Skills and Salaries
================================================================================

| Template | Primary Skills | Salary |
|---|---|---|
| Laborer | Knowledge-cooking, Athletics | 1500 |
| Medic | Medical Science | 3500 |
| Ruffian | Unarmed Attack, Melee Weapons | 1000 |
| Security Pro | Security, Ranged Weapons | 3500 |
| Soldier | Ranged Weapons | varies |
| Spacehand | System Operation, Vehicle Operation | 3000 |
| Steward | Administration, Culture | 2500 |
| Technician | Any Science, Technical Science | 4000 |
| Thug | Melee Weapons | 2000 |

(Note: Salaries are approximate monthly values. Some OCR artifacts may affect exact numbers.)

================================================================================
  #313 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 90
  A Cruel World
================================================================================

Each supporting character falls into one of five general categories: villains; allies and sidekicks; employees and followers; experts; and extras. Most scenarios feature at least one villain and a number of extras. The appearance of other supporting characters depends on the heroes' choices and the decisions the GM has made about the setting.

================================================================================
  #314 | TABLE | GMG Page 91
  Villain Power Level Guidelines
================================================================================

For a group of heroes averaging achievement level 5:

| Villain Type | Level Range | Description |
|---|---|---|
| Minor villain | 3-6 | A match for one hero alone |
| Major villain | 8-8 (sic; likely 5-8) | With special advantages or resources; a match for the entire party |
| Epic villain | 10-15 | Numerous underlings, exceptional resources, clear advantage over heroes on their best day |

A villain doesn't have to be physically superior -- positional power (authority, connections, supporters) can elevate a minor villain to major or epic status.

================================================================================
  #317 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 97
  Supporting Character Templates
================================================================================

Several templates for typical supporting characters of different power and experience level are presented. Each template includes vital statistics for typical representatives of certain careers of Marginal, Ordinary, Good, and Amazing quality, including Ability Scores, action check scores, number of actions per round, key skills, and signature equipment.

- **Marginal characters** — average members of society — are nonprofessionals. Average Ability Score of 9, small skill list. Employ as extras.
- **Ordinary characters** have capabilities roughly equivalent to a beginning hero (level 1). Average of 10 points in each Ability Score. Can be minor members of supporting cast.
- **Good characters** wield power and versatility equivalent to level 6 heroes. Average Ability Score is 11 points. Major members of the supporting cast.
- **Amazing characters** are figures to be respected or feared. Equivalent in power to level 12 heroes. Average of 12 points in each Ability Score. Used only in extraordinary circumstances.

More powerful characters possess all the skills listed for inferior characters. For example, a Good character has Marginal, Ordinary, and Good skills.

================================================================================
  #332 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 105-106
  Resource Contacts
================================================================================

A resource contact can provide equipment, money, personnel, or transportation. A soldier hero may not be able to take his battle armor into a starport under normal conditions, but a resource contact might be able to obtain a suit for special training purposes. Resource contacts may have subordinates whose services a hero needs. The contact might get upset if the hero is careless or indiscreet with the resource.

================================================================================
  #333 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 106
  Sample Allegiances
================================================================================

Allegiances are ties to larger organizations. A hero may be subject to orders and policies that restrict actions and force compliance. People who don't care for the hero's organization won't think much of the hero either. Agents of rival organizations view him as an enemy. The Gamemaster can use allegiances as a ready means to direct a hero into adventures.

Using contacts/allegiances generally does not require a skill check for normal requests. A skill check (Interaction, Business, Street Smart, Administration) may be required for exceptionally sensitive information, unusual resources, or use outside normal territory/jurisdiction.

Grade of success governs assistance:
- **Critical Failure**: No help forthcoming.
- **Marginal**: Information partial or outdated, resources delayed or inadequate.
- **Ordinary**: Information sufficient to steer heroes toward next goal; resources fulfill needs.
- **Good**: Information detailed and accurate; top-notch personnel or exceptionally fine equipment.
- **Amazing**: Extremely accurate information granting significant advantage; resources well in excess of need.

================================================================================
  #337 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 112
  Achievement Points Guidelines
================================================================================

Guidelines for awarding achievement points:
- 1 to 2 achievement points per adventure is fair as an award for each hero in the group; if the adventure is long or especially dramatic, award 1 point per two or three game sessions.
- Award an individual bonus of 1 point if a player depicts his hero's motivation, moral attitude, and character traits particularly well.
- Award an individual bonus of 1 point if a hero did something truly spectacular, noble, self-sacrificing, or heroic.

Example: If your group plays once or twice a week, and an adventure takes four sessions to complete, you would hand out 4 to 6 achievement points per month of continuing play.

================================================================================
  #338 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 119
  When Your Heroes Split Up
================================================================================

Advice on handling situations when heroes split up during a game session. When heroes separate, the Gamemaster must manage multiple concurrent scenes, alternating attention between groups. Methods include: switching between groups at natural break points, keeping individual scenes short to maintain engagement, and using cliffhangers when switching focus.

================================================================================
  #339 | TABLE | GMG Page 122
  G27: Challenge Time Frames
================================================================================

Guidelines for determining the time interval between individual parts of a complex skill check.

| Challenge Type        | Duration        | Check Interval |
|----------------------|-----------------|----------------|
| Athletic feat        | 10 seconds      | 1/phase        |
| Picking a lock       | 10-60 seconds   | 1/round        |
| Setting a trap       | 1-10 minutes    | 1/minute       |
| Temporary repairs    | 10-60 minutes   | 1/10 min.      |
| Climbing a large cliff| 1-12 hours     | 1/6 hours      |
| Permanent repairs    | 12-48 hours     | 1/hour         |
| Minor construction   | 2-7 days        | 1/day          |
| Extended journey     | 7-60 days       | 1/week         |

================================================================================
  #340 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 126
  Extended Encounters
================================================================================

For multi-day encounters, use a complex skill check:
1. Set opening attitude (Hostile, Neutral, or Friendly).
2. Each day, character makes skill check: Ordinary = 1 success, Good = 2, Amazing = 3.
3. Shifting attitude by one category requires 6 successes.
4. Shifting by a second category requires 12 more successes.
5. Shifting by a third category requires 24 more successes.

It's a long and hard task to bring about radical shifts in a subject's attitude.

================================================================================
  #341 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 126
  Encounter Time Guidelines
================================================================================

- **One-liners**: Single phase. Deception-bluff and Interaction-intimidate.
- **Brief speeches**: Round to about a minute. Leadership-inspire, Interaction-taunt.
- **Simple transactions**: 1-5 minutes. Business, Administration, Street Smart, Interaction-bargain. (Important negotiations can drag on for weeks/months.)
- **Conversations**: Few minutes to few hours. Culture, Entertainment, Interaction-seduce, Investigate-interrogate.

| Thermal imager     | 5  | —   | —     | —      |
| Video scanner      | 6  | —   | —     | —      |

\* Increase base vehicle cost by 100%
\** Increase base vehicle cost by 50%

Key system details:
- **Ablative Module (PL 8)**: Provides 50 points of protective energy. Mortal weakens by 3, wound by 2, stun by 1. Recharges at 1 hr per 10 points.
- **Airtight config. (PL 5)**: Sealed for airtight operation with airlock. Man-hours of air equal to durability rating.
- **Camouflager (PL 8)**: +2 penalty to Awareness-perception checks at >10 meters.
- **Deflection module (PL 7)**: +2 resistance vs Good firepower, +4 vs Ordinary firepower, +1 vs Amazing firepower. No defense against collisions.
- **ECM pod (PL 5)**: System Operation-communications check: CF -1 bonus, F no mod, O +1 penalty, G +2 penalty, A +3 penalty.
- **Hi-power engine (PL 5)**: +20% to cruising speed, max speed, and acceleration. Doubles vehicle base cost per purchase.
- **Medical suite (PL 5)**: Provides -2 bonus to Medical Science skill checks.
- **Performance package (PL 5)**: Drive rating improves by -1. Can be purchased up to 3 times. Each costs +50% vehicle cost.
- **Security system (PL 5)**: +3 penalty to intruder's Security/Manipulation checks.
- **Sonar (PL 5)**: Active mode -2 bonus but reveals position. Passive mode normal.
- **Stealth config. (PL 6)**: +3 penalty to enemy radar/IR detection checks.
- **Video scanner (PL 6)**: -2 bonus to skill checks for spotting concealed vehicles.

================================================================================
  #343 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 129
  ECM Pod Details (Vehicular)
================================================================================

ECM pod detects and jams enemy radar transmissions. Functions as EM detector and blocks incoming radar signals. Useful against missile guidance and fire control radars.

System Operation-communications skill check results:
- **Critical Failure**: -1 bonus (helps enemy)
- **Failure**: no modifier
- **Ordinary**: +1 penalty to enemy
- **Good**: +2 penalty
- **Amazing**: +3 penalty

================================================================================
  #351 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 139
  Vehicle Explosion Damage
================================================================================

On a Critical Failure durability check when a vehicle sustains mortal damage, the vehicle explodes:
- Passengers suffer d8+1 mortal points of energy (En) damage
- Characters within 6 meters suffer 2d6+1w
- Characters within 12 meters suffer d8-1w

  #356 | TABLE | GMG Page 144
  G37: Solar Cells
================================================================================

Power output of solar cells based on distance from nearest star.

| Distance   | Condition | Power/Cell |
|-----------|-----------|------------|

| 0.5-5 AU  | Good      | 4/cell     |
| 5-50 AU   | Ordinary  | 2/cell     |
| 50 AU+    | Marginal  | 0+         |

Cells may be powered artificially by lasers along star lanes (provides Amazing conditions).

================================================================================
  #357 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 144
  Reentry Capsules, Escape Pods, & Boarding Pods
================================================================================

Three types of small craft that can be included in any compartment:
- **Reentry capsule**: Allows crew to safely return to a planet's surface.
- **Escape pod**: Emergency evacuation craft for crew.
- **Boarding pod**: Used for boarding enemy vessels.

Each uses 1 durability point built into hull.

================================================================================
  #358 | TABLE | GMG Page 145
  G38: Ship Maneuverability
================================================================================

Cross-references ship durability with movement points generated to determine maneuver rating.

| Durability | 1 | 2-3 | 3-4 | 5-6 | 6-7 | 6-8  |
|-----------|---|-----|-----|-----|-----|------|
| 10+       | — | —   | —   | —   | —   | -1   |
| 20-35     | — | —   | —   | —   | —   | —    |
| 30+       | — | —   | —   | —   | —   | —    |

Movement Points vs. Durability determines the maneuver rating (bonus/penalty to Vehicle Operation-space vehicle skill checks).

Approximate maneuver ratings:
- Low movement points relative to durability: +3 to +1 penalty
- Balanced: 0 (no modifier)
- High movement points relative to durability: -1 to -2 bonus

================================================================================
  #362 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 147
  Other Drive Systems
================================================================================

The stardrive requires the presence and immense energy output of a mass reactor. It is a modification to a mass reactor consisting of a special set of inversion coils and a tachyon injection system. The stardrive itself is only 3 durability points but demands huge power from a mass reactor. Ships typically power down all other systems before using the stardrive.

The drivewave (PL 8) is an improvement that covers the vessel with a controlled energy field before entering drivespace, completing starfall in only 11 hours instead of 5 days.

================================================================================
  #364 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 150
  Jammer Defense System Details
================================================================================

Jammer (ECM) system skill check results and modifiers:
- **Critical Failure**: -2 bonus (helps enemy)
- **Failure**: no modifier
- **Ordinary**: +1 penalty to enemy sensors/comms/missiles
- **Good**: +2 penalty
- **Amazing**: +3 penalty

At PL 7, jammer also scrambles gravimetric frequencies, disturbing mass detectors and mass transceivers. Modifiers are cumulative.

================================================================================
  #365 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 150
  Deflection Inducer Defense Details
================================================================================

Creates belts of gravitational force to deflect projectiles and bend beam weapons. Skill check results:
- **Critical Failure**: -2 bonus (helps enemy)
- **Failure**: no modifier
- **Ordinary**: +1 penalty to attacker
- **Good**: +2 penalty
- **Amazing**: +3 penalty

Penalties doubled against non-spaceship weapons. Each system protects 20 durability points; without full coverage, no benefits.

================================================================================
  #366 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 150
  Damage Control System Levels
================================================================================

Damage control systems come in three quality levels:
- **Ordinary**: -1 bonus to durability checks, cost $50K/system
- **Good**: -2 bonus to durability checks, cost $200K/system
- **Amazing**: -3 bonus to durability checks, cost $500K/system

Each system requires 1 durability and 1 power factor, and protects compartments totaling 20 durability or less.

================================================================================
  #367 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 150
  Point-Defense Gun Details
================================================================================

Automated missile defense system using slugs, laser bursts, or maser bolts. Fires in all directions. On successful System Operation-defenses skill check, one incoming missile destroyed. Can also be used as a weapon with statistics equivalent to a laser cannon but dealing HI damage.

================================================================================
  #368 | TABLE | GMG Page 151
  G43: Shipboard Computer Systems
================================================================================

Dedicated computer systems and their costs. All require a computer core of the appropriate quality.

| System          | Cost  |
|-----------------|-------|
| Computer Core   | 50K   |
| Battle          | 50K   |
| Communications  | 10K   |
| Defense         | 25K   |
| Engineering     | 25K   |
| Navigation      | 10K   |
| Science         | 10K   |
| Sensors         | 10K   |

Quality levels:
- **Ordinary**: -1 skill bonus, requires Ordinary computer core
- **Good**: -2 skill bonus, requires Good computer core
- **Amazing**: -3 skill bonus, requires Amazing computer core

PL 6 computers limited to Ordinary quality. PL 7+ can reach Good and Amazing quality.

================================================================================
  #369 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 151
  Displacer Defense Details
================================================================================

A refinement of the inertial flux engine unit. When triggered, the ship executes a slide of a few hundred meters. Skill check results:
- **Critical Failure**: -1 bonus (helps enemy)
- **Marginal**: +1 penalty to attacker
- **Ordinary**: +2 penalty
- **Good**: +3 penalty
- **Amazing**: +4 penalty

================================================================================
  #370 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 151
  Ablative Shield Defense Details
================================================================================

Envelops ship with a field of quantum particles. Engineer devotes power factors to the unit each phase. Damage absorption:
- Every point of mortal damage reduces the field by 3 points
- Every point of wound damage reduces the field by 2 points
- Every point of stun damage reduces the field by 1 point

Primary damage absorbed does not cause secondary damage.

================================================================================
  #372 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 155
  Measurements
================================================================================

Key measurements for spaceship operations:
- **Mm** = Megameter = 1,000 km = 1 million meters
- **Mpp** = Megameters per phase = 1 million kilometers per hour
- **AU** = Astronomical Unit = 150 million km (Earth-Sun distance)
- **c** = speed of light = approximately 300,000 km/s = about 8 AU/hour

================================================================================

================================================================================
  #374 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 156
  Stardrive Recharge Time
================================================================================

After making starfall, a driveship needs to accumulate a tachyonic charge before reentering drivespace. Three methods to determine recharge time:
1. Roll d4+1 for number of days.
2. Roll 7d12+36 for number of hours (more precise).
3. Allow engineer to attempt System Operation-engineering skill check to decrease time:
   - Ordinary: 6d12+36 hours
   - Good: 5d12+36 hours
   - Amazing: 4d12+36 hours
   - Rank benefit (4+ ranks in engineering): reduce by additional d12

================================================================================
  #380 | TABLE | GMG Page 160
  G49: Losing Control of a Spaceship
================================================================================

When a pilot fails a Vehicle Operation skill check, a second check determines the outcome.

| Skill Check Result | Outcome        |
|-------------------|----------------|
| Critical Failure  | Major spin     |
| Failure           | Spin           |
| Ordinary          | Yaw            |
| Good              | Under control  |
| Amazing           | Under control  |

**Major spin**: Ship enters spin with +4 penalty on regain attempts; +2 penalty to all crew actions. May crash near large objects.
**Spin**: Ship goes wildly out of control. Roll d8 for final facing. Pilot can't do anything else until control regained. All crew suffer +2 penalty.
**Yaw**: Vehicle slides at an angle (roll d6: 1-3 right, 4-6 left). Continues until pilot's next action.
**Under control**: No trouble; continues on course.

If already in a spin and fails again with any result other than "Under control," enters major spin.

================================================================================
  #381 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 160
  Copilot Skills (Spaceship Combat)
================================================================================

The copilot can take over piloting at any time (with +1 penalty from copilot station). Alternatively, the copilot can take an action to assist the pilot's maneuvering. The copilot's Vehicle Operation-space vehicle check determines the modifier to the pilot's next skill check:
- **Critical Failure**: +1 penalty
- **Failure**: no modifier
- **Ordinary**: -1 bonus
- **Good**: -2 bonus
- **Amazing**: -3 bonus

================================================================================
  #382 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 161-162
  Sensor Assistance in Combat
================================================================================

Sensors can assist attacks in two ways:

**1. Improve hit odds**: Sensors operator spends action; skill check provides modifier to weapons operator in next phase:
- Critical Failure: +2 penalty
- Failure: no modifier
- Ordinary: -1 bonus
- Good: -2 bonus
- Amazing: -3 bonus

**2. Target specific compartment**: Sensors operator must have action in same phase as successful shot. Skill check allows adjusting random d20 compartment hit roll:
- Critical Failure: shot misses entirely
- Failure: no modifier
- Ordinary: adjust roll by 1
- Good: adjust roll by 2
- Amazing: adjust roll by 3

**3. Assist defenses**: Sensors operator spends action; modifier applies for rest of current round and all of next round:
- Critical Failure: +2 penalty
- Failure: no modifier
- Ordinary: -1 bonus
- Good: -2 bonus
- Amazing: -3 bonus

================================================================================
  #383 | TABLE | GMG Page 162
  G50: Compartment Hit Location
================================================================================

When a ship is hit, roll d20 and refer to the column for the ship's number of compartments. The number in that column is the number of the compartment that was hit.

(This is an asymmetric hit location table designed so higher-numbered/outer compartments are hit more often, protecting vital inner systems. Sensor operators can adjust the d20 roll by their skill check result to target specific compartments.)

================================================================================
  #384 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 162-163
  Spaceship Damage and Toughness
================================================================================

All spaceships have Amazing toughness:
- **Good firepower weapons** (most heavy/vehicular weapons): damage degrades one grade (mortal becomes wound, wound becomes stun, stun ignored)
- **Ordinary firepower weapons** (most personal weapons): damage degrades twice (mortal becomes stun, wound and stun ignored)

Example: A 9mm pistol must score an Amazing hit (which inflicts mortal damage, degraded to stun) to affect a ship at all.

================================================================================
  #385 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 162
  Command Skills in Spaceship Combat
================================================================================

Commander can use Tactics-space tactics skill check to provide modifier to crew's next action checks:
- **Critical Failure**: +2 penalty for all other crew members
- **Failure**: no modifier
- **Ordinary**: -1 bonus for one other crew member
- **Good**: -1 bonus for all other crew members
- **Amazing**: -2 bonus for all other crew members

================================================================================
  #386 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 162
  Communication Skills in Spaceship Combat
================================================================================

Comm officer can code messages. Skill check provides modifier to enemy decoding attempts:
- **Critical Failure**: -2 bonus (helps enemy)
- **Failure**: no modifier
- **Ordinary**: +1 penalty to enemy
- **Good**: +2 penalty
- **Amazing**: +3 penalty

Can also spend action jamming enemy transmissions (modifiers apply to opponent's comms and sensor checks next round).

================================================================================
  #387 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 164
  Damage to Passengers and Crew
================================================================================

When a compartment suffers damage, individuals inside suffer the same primary damage reduced one grade. Armor is accounted for first. Damage suffered by passengers and crew is low impact (LI).

Example: Wallace is in a compartment hit for 8 wound damage. Armor absorbs 5, leaving 3 wound damage. Wallace takes 3 stun damage (one grade less).

Characters in completely destroyed compartments may suffer decompression effects.

================================================================================
  #388 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 164-165
  Damage Control Repair Complexities
================================================================================

Full repair complexity requirements:
- **Stun damage**: Ordinary complexity, 3 successes, 1 attempt per round of work
- **Wound damage**: Good complexity, 4 successes; attempts once per minute (if <= half wound rating lost) or once per hour (if > half wound rating lost)
- **Mortal damage**: Amazing complexity, 8 successes + 1 per mortal point; attempts once per day

Juryrigging side effects on full repairs:
- Ordinary juryrig result: 3 additional successes needed
- Good juryrig result: 2 additional successes needed
- Amazing juryrig result: 1 additional success needed

Compartments that have lost all mortal boxes cannot be repaired; must be replaced.

================================================================================
  #389 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 164
  Engineering Skills in Spaceship Combat
================================================================================

Engineering officer functions:
1. **Power allocation**: With an action, freely allocate ship's power factors to systems.
2. **Remote repair** (stun damage only): System Operation-engineering skill check:
   - Critical Failure: compartment suffers d4 stun damage
   - Failure: no stun points repaired
   - Ordinary: 1 stun point repaired
   - Good: 2 stun points repaired
   - Amazing: 3 stun points repaired
3. **Assist damage control**: Provides modifier to damage control officer's next repair attempt:
   - Critical Failure: +2 penalty
   - Failure: no modifier
   - Ordinary: -1 bonus
   - Good: -2 bonus
   - Amazing: -3 bonus

================================================================================
  #390 | TABLE | GMG Page 167
  G51: Alien Artifact Form
================================================================================

Roll d20 to determine the physical form of an alien artifact.

| d20   | Form                               |
|-------|-------------------------------------|
| 1-3   | Appliance or Machine                |
| 4-9   | Carried device (roll d20 sub-table) |
| 10-14 | Clothing/Worn device (roll d20 sub-table) |
| 15    | Graft or Implant (roll d20 sub-table) |

================================================================================
  #394 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 169
  Artifact Power: Analysis
================================================================================

The artifact provides a detailed analysis of any object or area scanned. Range of 20 meters, affecting one target at a time or an area 6 meters in diameter. Provides -3 bonus to any Science or Investigate skill checks.

- **Ordinary**: All energy forms and relationships analyzed with complete accuracy.
- **Good**: Energy and inanimate matter/compounds analyzed with complete accuracy.
- **Amazing**: Energy, inanimate matter, and living organisms analyzed with complete accuracy.

================================================================================
  #395 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 169
  Artifact Power: Anti-life Ray
================================================================================

Beam of energy disrupting bioelectric energy. Fired using Modern Ranged Weapons skill. On hit: d6w/2d4w/3d4w of energy (En) damage at Ordinary firepower. Armor useless against it.

- **Ordinary**: Single target, 20 meters range, once per day.
- **Good**: All targets in 1m wide, 40m long path, three times per day.
- **Amazing**: All targets in 2m wide, 60m long path, six times per day.

================================================================================
  #396 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 169
  Artifact Power: Armor
================================================================================

Device can be worn as armor or toughen the wearer's body. If combined with other armor, only the more effective armor is considered.

- **Ordinary**: Absorbs d6+1 hits against any attack.
- **Good**: Absorbs 2d4 hits and provides Good toughness.
- **Amazing**: Absorbs 2d4+1 hits and provides Amazing toughness.

================================================================================
  #397 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 169-170
  Artifact Power: Carrier Wave
================================================================================

Converts user into an energy form for rapid travel. Forms include: electrical (along wires), light/radiation (line of sight), sound/seismic (through water/solids), psionic (all mediums, detectable by Mindwalkers).

If the hero encounters interference (short in wire, smoke, radiation shielding), hero materializes at that point or returns to departure.

- **Ordinary**: Once per day, up to 1 minute.
- **Good**: Four times per day, up to 10 minutes each.
- **Amazing**: Once every 2 hours, up to 15 minutes each.

================================================================================
  #399 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 170
  Artifact Power: Cyberconscious
================================================================================

Functions as a gridcaster, allowing the hero to project consciousness into computers, networks, and computerized machinery. Uses Knowledge-computer operation skill.

- **Ordinary**: -2 bonus, must be in contact with target computer.
- **Good**: Range 500 meters, -3 step bonus.
- **Amazing**: Range 50 kilometers, -4 step bonus.

================================================================================
  #400 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 170
  Artifact Power: Cybercontrol
================================================================================

Hero can exert control over any computer or computerized machinery. Uses Knowledge-computer operation skill check.

Results:
- **Ordinary success**: Device operation interrupted, +2 penalty or temporary failure.
- **Good success**: Device controlled for duration of concentration.
- **Amazing success**: Commands remain in place until someone repairs the device.

Can be used at will with an action. Hero must see the target device.

- **Ordinary**: -2 bonus, 10 meters range.
- **Good**: -3 bonus, 100 meters range.
- **Amazing**: -4 bonus, 1 kilometer range.

================================================================================
  #401 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 170
  Artifact Power: Dark Matter Attack
================================================================================

Once per hour, the hero can condense streams of dark matter into bolts or blades. Uses Modern Ranged Weapons skill check.

- **Ordinary**: 2d4s/2d4w/d8m of En/G damage, 100 meters range.
- **Good**: 3d4s/3d4w/2d4m of En/G damage, 200 meters range.
- **Amazing**: (continues on page 171)
