================================================================================
  #408 | TABLE | GMG Page 196
  G62: Planets
================================================================================

Determines planet type, number of moons, and moon modifier from a die result.

| Die Result | Type | Moons | Moon Modifier |
|---|---|---|---|
| -- | Ring system | None | N/A |
| 1 | Super-Terran, hot | d6-3 | -5 |
| 2 | Sub-Terran | d6-3 | -5 |
| 3 | Terran, hot | d6-4 | -3 |
| 4 | Terran, temperate | d6-2 | -3 |
| 5 | Sub-Terran, temperate | d6-3 | -- |
| 6 | Super-Terran, temperate | d8-3 | -- |
| 7 | Asteroid belt | None | -- |
| 8 | Gas giant | 2d6+2 | -- |
| 9 | Gas giant, small | d12 | -- |
| 10 | Super-Terran, cold | d6 | -- |
| 11 | Terran, cold | d4 | -- |
| 12 | Sub-Terran, cold | d3 | -- |
| 13+ | Comet belt | -- | -- |

Notes: Type defines the planetary body. Moons indicates the number of moons the body possesses. A result less than 1 indicates an absence of moons. For each moon that exists, roll once on Table G63: Moons. Moon Modifier lists a modifier that applies to the 2d6 roll made on Table G63.

================================================================================
  #409 | TABLE | GMG Page 196
  G63: Moons
================================================================================

Roll 2d6 (plus Moon Modifier from Table G62) to determine the type of each moon.

| 2d6 Result | Type |
|---|---|
| 2 or less | Tiny |
| 3-4 | Small |
| 5-7 | Ring system |
| 8-9 | Sub-Terran |
| 10-11 | Terran |
| 12+ | Super-Terran |

Notes: A moon has the same temperature as its parent planet. Consider gas giants to be cold -- but see the text for an exception (large moons of gas giants orbiting close to their star may be temperate).

================================================================================
  #411 | TABLE | GMG Page 201
  G65: Oceans
================================================================================

Roll d8 and cross-reference with planet environment class to determine extent of oceans.

| d8 Roll | Class 1 | Class 2 | Class 3 |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1-2 | Sparse | None | None |
| 3-4 | Moderate | Sparse | None |
| 5-6 | Abundant | Moderate | Sparse |
| 7-8 | Complete | Abundant | Moderate |

Ocean types:
- Sparse: small landlocked seas or frozen ice caps, covering about one-quarter of the planet.
- Moderate: large landlocked seas or extensive ice caps, covering roughly half the planet.
- Abundant: cover most of the planet's surface, dividing continents from each other.
- Complete: cover the planet, with only a few islands rising above the waves.

================================================================================
  #412 | TABLE | GMG Page 201
  G66: Climate
================================================================================

Roll d8 and cross-reference with planet environment class to determine climate severity.

| d8 Roll | Class 1 | Class 2 | Class 3 |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1-2 | Calm | Calm | Active |
| 3-5 | Active | Active | Turbulent |
| 6-7 | Turbulent | Turbulent | Violent |
| 8+ | Violent | Violent | Violent |

Notes: Add 1 to the die roll if the planet has sparse oceans or no oceans, and add an additional 3 if the planet is a gas giant. If the planet has an extreme axial tilt or a fast rotation rate, add 1 for each. If the planet has a mild axial tilt or a slow rotation rate, subtract 1 for each.

Climate types:
- Calm: placid by Earth standards, little variation, infrequent storms, gentle winds.
- Active: similar to Earth -- distinct seasons, intense winds and storms, surface temperature fluctuates by as much as 100 degrees C.
- Turbulent: wider range of temperatures, more powerful storms and winds than active. Mars is an example.
- Violent: drastic temperature range, constant storms, destructive winds. Saturn and Neptune are examples.

================================================================================
  #413 | TABLE | GMG Page 202
  G67: Landforms
================================================================================

Roll d8 and cross-reference with planet environment class to determine landform profile.

| d8 Roll | Class 1 | Class 2 | Class 3 |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1-3 | Smooth | Smooth | Smooth |
| 4-5 | Varied | Smooth | Smooth |
| 6-7 | Varied | Varied | Rugged |
| 8+ | Rugged | Rugged | Perilous |

Notes: Disregard landforms for gas giants (no land). If the planet has one or more moons or is a sub-Terran world, add 1 to the die roll. If the planet is a super-Terran, or has a corrosive (A4) or super corrosive (A5) atmosphere, subtract 1.

Landform types:
- Smooth: geological landscape less pronounced than Earth's. Low flat mountains, shallow seas, little volcanic activity. Venus is an example.
- Varied: about the same range as Earth's, with active plate tectonics and moderate volcanism.
- Rugged: significantly more exaggerated than Earth's. Higher and sheerer mountains. Mars is an example.
- Perilous: even more pronounced than rugged. Very light gravity or extreme tidal forces may seriously deform a planet's crust.

================================================================================
  #414 | TABLE | GMG Page 203
  G68: Lifeforms
================================================================================

Determines the biochemical series of life that might exist on a planet. Roll d8; if the result falls within the given range, life of that series exists.

| Series | Breathes | Odds (d8) |
|---|---|---|
| I | Carbon / Oxygen | 1-2 |
| II | Carbon / Hydrogen | 1 |
| III | Silicone / Chlorine | 1 |
| IV | Carbon / Sulfur trioxide | 1-2 |
| V | Carbon / Oxygen | 1 |
| VI | Carbon / Sulfur dioxide | 1 |

Notes: If a planet is capable of supporting native life, the "Life" column on Table G64 lists one or two series. Then roll d8 on this table. If life exists, there is a 75% chance (1-6 on d8) that it is too simple (primordial) to be anything more than scientifically interesting.

================================================================================
  #415 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 203-204
  Organizing Lifeforms -- Five Categories
================================================================================

When heroes explore a new planet, describe lifeforms that fall into one of five general categories:
1. Aggressive carnivores or scavengers.
2. Aggressive herbivores that actively defend themselves from perceived threats.
3. Plants and animals with passive defense mechanisms that may prove dangerous.
4. Pests, vermin, or parasites that may attack through blind instinct.
5. Creatures of scientific interest or with unusual properties.

If a creature isn't going to attack the heroes and doesn't possess anything useful, you don't have to spend time detailing it.

================================================================================
  #416 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 204-205
  Civilization Level (CL 0-8)
================================================================================

Civilization Level is a rough measurement of the extent to which a world has been settled.

| CL | Name | Population | Resource Modifier |
|---|---|---|---|
| 0 | Uninhabited | None | Auto-fail |
| 1 | Unique | ~1,000 | +3 penalty |
| 2 | Scattered | ~10,000 | +2 penalty |
| 3 | City | 100,000+ | +1 penalty |
| 4 | Nation | 1-10 million | No modifier |
| 5 | Continent | ~100 million | -1 bonus |
| 6 | World | ~1 billion | -2 bonus |
| 7 | Improved World | ~10 billion | -3 bonus |
| 8 | Megapolitan World | 25-50 billion | -4 bonus |

================================================================================
  #417 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 205-206
  Law Level (LL 0-8)
================================================================================

Law Level describes a civilization's government in terms of organization and power. Each level has a modifier that applies when heroes attempt illegal acts.

| LL | Name | Modifier | Description |
|---|---|---|---|
| 0 | Anarchy | -4 | No law exists except the law of the jungle. |
| 1 | Tribal | -3 | No universal rules of conduct; local groups may develop codes. |
| 2 | Feudal | -2 | Law serves individuals in power. Corruption is rife. |
| 3 | Civic | -1 | Basic standard of conduct, elementary civil rights, some police. |
| 4 | State | 0 | Common laws and enforcement agencies. Corruption is modest. |
| 5 | National | +1 | Like the United States of the 1990s. Specialized law organizations. |
| 6 | Totalitarian | +2 | Authorities may use or disregard civil rights as they see fit. |
| 7 | Technocracy | +3 | Extensive surveillance, propaganda, and mind control. |
| 8 | Nonhuman | +4 | Inhabitants incapable of crime by design or nature. |

Notes: Reverse the modifier from a bonus to a penalty (or vice versa) if the heroes try to make use of a local law agency. A large civilization (CL 3 or higher) must have a Law Level equal to or greater than its Civilization Level or else the society falls into anarchy.

================================================================================
  #418 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 212
  Adventure Design Template
================================================================================

Summary outline for spontaneous or planned adventure design:
- Idea
- Background
- Supporting Cast
- The Trigger

================================================================================
  #419 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 214
  Three-Act Adventure Structure
================================================================================

The basic structure of a three-act adventure:

**Act One**
- Scene One: Trigger
- Scene Two: Complications
- Scene Three: Minor Resolution and Dramatic High Note

**Act Two**
- Scene One: Trigger
- Scene Two: Complications
- Scene Three: Minor Resolution and Dramatic High Note

**Act Three**
- Scene One: Trigger
- Scene Two: Complications
- Scene Three: Major Resolution and Climax

Alternates: Plan for two or three alternate paths that you can eventually use to get back to the main story.
- Alternate #1
- Alternate #2

================================================================================
  #420 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 216-217
  Adventure Hook #1: Hijacked!
================================================================================

Modern-day to near-future technothriller. Terrorists take control of a high-speed passenger train with the President aboard. Heroes must neutralize terrorists, save the President, and regain control before the train reaches the coast -- where the terrorists plan to detonate a nuclear device. Includes background, supporting cast notes, and a trigger scene.

================================================================================
  #421 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 217-218
  Adventure Hook #2: Installation 251
================================================================================

Contemporary horror SF tale. In a secret Alaskan government facility, an alien creature has escaped captivity and is systematically killing personnel. Heroes are sent to investigate. Includes background, supporting cast notes, and a trigger scene in which the base goes into quarantine lockdown.

================================================================================
  #422 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 218
  Adventure Hook #3: Murder on Asteroid 36
================================================================================

Near-future PL 6 adventure. A mining detail has uncovered an alien artifact on Asteroid 36 that possesses a malevolent aura driving miners insane and turning some into psychopathic murderers. Heroes must subdue the murderers and secure the artifact. Includes background, supporting cast notes, and a trigger scene.

================================================================================
  #423 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 218-219
  Adventure Hook #4: First Contact
================================================================================

Exploration or space opera campaign at PL 7+. The heroes' starship encounters an alien communication signal from an unknown species. Two alien ships -- one being chased and fired upon by another -- crash on a habitable planet. Heroes must investigate. Includes background, supporting cast notes, and a trigger scene.

================================================================================
  #424 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 220
  Mutants and Aliens (Optional Rule Note)
================================================================================

The mutation system presented in the Player's Handbook does not allow members of an alien species to play mutants. There's no reason you can't choose to allow certain alien races to indulge in genetic experimentation or random mutagenics. The factor you'll want to be aware of is the possibility of a weren hero with a Strength score of 18, or a fraal with an Intelligence score of 18.

================================================================================
  #425 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 220-221
  Four Options for Mutants in the Campaign
================================================================================

1. Mutant heroes don't exist. Mutations are usually harmful and often fatal.
2. Mutant powers are incredibly rare. Only a select few have access. Objects of scorn and scrutiny.
3. Mutants are simply uncommon. Most people know they exist. Social authorities have rules to accommodate them.
4. Everyone is a mutant (extreme option). Result of massive irradiation or alien tinkering.

================================================================================
  #426 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 221
  Four Options for Psionics in the Campaign
================================================================================

1. Psionic powers don't exist. ESP, clairvoyance, and telekinesis are hoaxes.
2. Psionic powers available only to a very limited or select group (rare psi-gene).
3. Psionic talents are uncommon but not unheard of. Man on the street knows about them.
4. Everyone possesses psionic powers. Mindwalker skills become Open skills.

================================================================================
  #427 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 222-223
  Three Options for Cybernetics in the Campaign
================================================================================

1. The technology doesn't exist. Neural interface technology has yet to be invented.
2. The technology exists but its use is morally questionable or requires exorbitant resources.
3. The technology exists and is widely available. Minor stylistic cybertech improvements are common.

================================================================================
  #428 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 222-223
  Three Options for Artificial Intelligence
================================================================================

1. AI is impossible. Computers resemble 20th century machines (faster but not sentient).
2. AI is possible but impractical. Built for special purposes, carefully controlled.
3. AIs are relatively common. Everyone has access to computers with decision-making abilities.

================================================================================
  #429 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 226
  FX Broad Skill Types
================================================================================

The three FX broad skills:
- Arcane Magic
- Faith
- Super Power

================================================================================
  #430 | TABLE | GMG Page 227
  G69: FX Broad Skill Costs
================================================================================

(Referenced in text.) Standard costs for the FX broad skills: Arcane Magic, Faith, and Super Power. The Gamemaster is free to modify the costs to fit the campaign.

================================================================================
  #431 | TABLE | GMG Page 227
  G70: Faith FX Specialty Skill Costs
================================================================================

Fixed costs for Faith FX specialty skills:
- Ordinary miracles: 5 skill points
- Good miracles: 10 skill points
- Amazing miracles: 15 skill points

================================================================================
  #432 | TABLE | GMG Page 227
  G71: Arcane Magic & Super Power FX Specialty Skill Costs
================================================================================

Add up varying effects to get a base cost for the FX specialty skill.

| FX Specialty Skill Effect | Cost |
|---|---|
| Ability Score boost (+1/+3/+5) | 5/10/15 |
| Bonus steps (-1/-2/-3) | 3/5/7 |
| Penalty steps (+1/+2/+3) | 3/5/7 |
| Bonus to damage (1/2/3 points) | 2/4/6 |
| Bonus to combat movement | 5/10/15 |
| Fatigue damage (1-4 points) | -- |
| Stun damage (1-5 points) | -- |
| Stun damage (6-10 points) | -- |
| Stun damage (11-15 points) | -- |
| Wound damage (1-5 points) | -- |
| Wound damage (6-10 points) | -- |
| Wound damage (11-15 points) | -- |
| Mortal damage (1-2 points) | -- |
| Mortal damage (3-5 points) | -- |
| Damage type (O/G/A) | -- |
| Low impact (LI) attack | -- |
| High impact (HI) attack | -- |
| Energy (En) attack | -- |
| Duration, instant | -- |
| Duration (1/2/3 time units) | -- |
| Flight or other special movement | -- |
| Knowledge | -- |
| Range, personal | -- |
| Range, 2/4/6 meters | -- |
| Range, 10/20/30 meters | -- |
| Range, 100/200/300 meters | -- |
| Range, 1/2/3 kilometers | -- |
| Travel (1 km/10 km/100 km) | -- |

Notes: FX specialty skills with a total base cost of 5 points or less are Ordinary quality; 6-10 points = Good quality; 11-15 points = Amazing quality. No FX specialty skill can have a base cost of more than 15 points. The quality determines its cost in FX energy to use.

================================================================================
  #433 | TABLE | GMG Page 229-230
  G72: FX Energy
================================================================================

FX Energy available by campaign tone.

| Campaign Tone | Starting | Max | Cost (per point) |
|---|---|---|---|
| Realistic | 5 | 10 | 20 |
| Heroic | 10 | 20 | -- |
| Super Heroic | 15 | 30 | -- |

Notes: Starting = the amount of FX energy a starting character with FX powers begins with. Max = the most FX energy a character can ever have. Cost = the skill points needed to purchase an extra point of energy.

================================================================================
  #435 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 230
  FX Examples -- Fate Casting
================================================================================

Arcane Magic, Augur spell: WIL; Good quality, base cost 6
This spell determines the possible fate of a character within the next 24 hours (6 pts); provides general information (3 pts); and requires the casting of runestones (-1 pt) over the course of a skill check of Good complexity (-2 pts).

================================================================================
  #436 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 230
  FX Examples -- Bolt of Lightning
================================================================================

Arcane Magic, Conjure spell: WIL; Good quality, base cost 8
This spell aims a bolt of lightning at a target (energy attack, 3 pts). It inflicts Ordinary damage (0 pts) of d4s/d4w/d4+2w (low stun 1 pt; low wound 2 pts). The bolt's range is 2/4/6 meters (2 pts). Trappings: wood shavings from a lightning-struck tree (-1 pt) and a skill check of Good complexity (-2 pts).

================================================================================
  #437 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 230
  FX Examples -- Fly
================================================================================

Arcane Magic, Summon spell: WIL; Good quality, base cost 9
This spell allows the caster to fly (6 pts) at a rate equal to his fly movement rate (see Table P8: Combat Movement Rates in the Player's Handbook). The flight lasts for 2 minutes (4 pts). Requires a component of soap bubbles (-1 pt) and a simple skill check.

================================================================================
  #438 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 230
  FX Examples -- Enchant Weapon
================================================================================

Arcane Magic, Transform spell: PER; Amazing quality, base cost 11
This spell temporarily bestows magical qualities upon an ordinary weapon. It provides a 3-point bonus to damage inflicted by the weapon (6 pts), and the weapon remains enchanted for 3 minutes (6 pts). Casting requires a component of silver dust sprinkled over the item (-1 pt) and a simple skill check.

================================================================================
  #439 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 230
  FX Examples -- Divine Guidance
================================================================================

Faith, Ordinary miracle: WIL; Ordinary quality, base cost 5
The character prays for advice concerning a particular course of action. The answer comes in the form of a feeling or sense of the rightness or wrongness of an action. The guidance is equivalent to general knowledge.

================================================================================
  #440 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 230
  FX Examples -- Divine Blessing
================================================================================

Faith, Good miracle: WIL; Good quality, base cost 10
When this prayer is answered, the miracle worker causes a divine agency to bestow a blessing: -1 bonus to the group's action checks and +1 to the group's resistance modifiers. The blessing remains in effect for 2 rounds.

================================================================================
  #441 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 230
  FX Examples -- Song of the Eagle
================================================================================

Faith, Amazing miracle: WIL; Amazing quality, base cost 15
This prayer is answered by changing the miracle worker into an eagle for 1 hour. As an eagle, the character retains his own Intelligence and memories. Durability rating of 6/6/3. Once knocked unconscious or out of mortal points, the character returns to normal form; damage suffered in eagle form remains.

================================================================================
  #442 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 230
  FX Examples -- Cloak of Invisibility
================================================================================

Super Power, Relic: DEX; Amazing quality, base cost 12
When the word of power is spoken, the cloak turns its wearer invisible. Provides a -3 bonus (7 pts) to all Stealth checks and adds +2 to resistance modifiers for any attacks requiring sight of the target (5 pts).

================================================================================
  #443 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 230
  FX Examples -- Strength of the Behemoth
================================================================================

Super Power, Extreme Ability: CON; Good quality, base cost 8
This power increases the character's Strength score by as much as 3 (10 pts) for as long as the FX energy lasts. Every round uses 2 FX energy points. Degree of success indicates actual Strength increase (+1/+2/+3). Limitation: in the cold (0 degrees C or less), the check is made with a +1 penalty (-1 pt).

================================================================================
  #444 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 230
  FX Examples -- Web Spinneret
================================================================================

Super Power, Overscience gadget: DEX; Ordinary quality, base cost 2
An overscience device worn around the character's wrist. Fires a line of superstrong, ultrathin material that sticks to a distant object. Range 10/20/30 meters (4 pts), with +2 and +3 penalty for medium and long range. Webline has effective Strength score of 16. Requires Technical Science-repair skill check of Good complexity to replenish (-2 pts).

================================================================================
  #445 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 232
  Animal & Alien Statistics Explanation
================================================================================

Explains how animal and alien creature statistics work:
- Ability Scores: a single value for each, with a range in parentheses for individualization (e.g., STR 16 (d6+12)).
- Intelligence and Personality use an "Animal" scale (e.g., "INT 3 (Animal 11 or d4+9)") -- the Animal value is the effective score for animal-appropriate tasks.
- Attacks and Defenses: use +d0 base situation die. Predators have higher attack scores.
- Skills: broad skills with scores in brackets, specialty skills likewise (e.g., "Athletics [16]-climb [18]").

================================================================================
  #446 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 233
  Animals Combat Behavior
================================================================================

Animals don't attack just because a human crosses their path. They attack because they're frightened, angered, startled, or (rarely) hungry. Unless actively hunting, animals engage in warning displays (growling, bluffing a charge, beating its chest). If an animal does stalk a hero, it uses Stealth to surprise. Large animals often try to knock targets flat first. An animal with several attack options can try one of each as a single action. Few animals fight to the death.

================================================================================
  #482 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 244-245
  AD&D to Alternity Conversion -- Race/Species Abilities
================================================================================

Conversion rules for AD&D character races to Alternity:

**Dwarves:** Free broad skills: Athletics, Stamina, Knowledge, Awareness, Resolve, Interaction. Magic and Poison Resistance (+2 resistance modifier vs Arcane Magic/Faith FX; -2 bonus to Con feat checks vs poison/radiation). Defensive Skill (+2 vs melee/unarmed from humanoids 3+ meters tall). Infravision. Mining Skills (Will-based broad skill: detect grade/slope -2 step bonus, detect new construction -2 step bonus, detect sliding/shifting walls -1 step bonus, detect stonework traps no modifier, detect depth no modifier).

**Elves:** Free broad skills: Athletics, Melee Weapons or Primitive Ranged Weapons, Stealth, Knowledge, Awareness, Interaction. Charm Resistance (+4 vs charm/sleep FX). Infravision. Secret Door Detection (-2 bonus to Investigate-search).

**Gnomes:** Free broad skills: Athletics, Stamina, Manipulation, Knowledge, Awareness, Interaction. Magic Resistance (+2 vs Arcane Magic/Faith FX). Defensive Skills (+2 vs melee/unarmed from humanoids 2.5+ meters tall). Infravision. Mining Skills (same as Dwarves).

**Halflings:** Free broad skills: Stamina, Stealth, Knowledge, Awareness, Resolve, Interaction. Magic and Poison Resistance (+2 vs Arcane Magic/Faith FX; -2 bonus to Con feat checks vs poison/radiation). Throwing Bonus (-1 bonus to Athletics-throw). Infravision (stout halflings full; mixed halflings negate up to +2 penalties).

**Half-elves:** Free broad skills: Athletics, Stealth, Stamina, Knowledge, Awareness, Interaction. Charm Resistance (+2 vs charm/sleep FX). Infravision. Secret Door Detection (-1 bonus to Investigate-search).

================================================================================
  #483 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 245
  AD&D to Alternity Conversion -- Class to Profession
================================================================================

| AD&D Class | Alternity Profession |
|---|---|
| Fighter | Combat Spec |
| Paladin | Combat Spec |
| Ranger | Combat Spec |
| Cleric | Diplomat |
| Druid | Diplomat |
| Thief | Free Agent |
| Bard | Diplomat |
| Mage | Tech Op |
| Specialist Wizard | Tech Op |

================================================================================
  #484 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 247
  AD&D Spellcasting Conversion
================================================================================

Conversion rules for spellcasters in a magical universe:
- Wizards, clerics, druids, specialty priests: 7 spell points per level for FX specialty skills.
- Rangers: 5 points per level above 8th.
- Paladins: 5 points per level above 9th.
- These spell points can only be used for FX specialty skills.
- Each AD&D spell must be converted to an FX ability using the FX rules from Chapter 16.
- A 2-point penalty in the AD&D system is roughly equal to a 1-step penalty in the Alternity rules.

================================================================================
  #485 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 247
  Magic Missile FX Conversion Example
================================================================================

Magic Missile -- Arcane Magic, Conjure spell: WIL; Ordinary quality, cost 9
Allows caster to manipulate energy into small bolts that inflict Ordinary Energy (En) damage. Skill check determines damage: Critical Failure = random target; Marginal = d4-2w (min 1); Ordinary = d4-1w; Good = d4w; Amazing = d4+1w. Ranges 10/20/30 meters. -1 bonus at short, no modifier at medium, +1 penalty at long. Extra missile at skill ranks 3, 6, 9, and 12.

================================================================================
  #487 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 253-254
  System Record Form (Ship Record Form)
================================================================================

Two pages of blank record forms:
- **Page 253**: System Record Form for recording star system details. Includes orbit rings for planet placement, with fields for planet type and orbital distance.
- **Page 254**: Ship Status Record Form. Fields include: Hull size, Maneuver rating, Ship name, Hull HP, Cruising speed, Captain's name, Starfall distance. Ship Stations table (Command, Pilot, Copilot, Sensors, Communications, Damage Control, Defenses, Engineering, Weapons) each with Location, Operator's Name, System, Skill Score. Compartments 1-12 each with S/W/M durability tracking circles.

================================================================================
  #488 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 255
  Supporting Cast Statistical Form (Explained)
================================================================================

A full-page annotated example of the Supporting Cast Statistical Form, using the character "Yatril Tor" (Level 1 human Diplomat/Mindwalker) as a demonstration. The form layout includes:
- Character name, species, profession, achievement level
- Ability Scores with resistance modifiers
- Durability, action check, movement rates, actions per round, reaction score, last resort points
- Perks and Flaws
- Psionic energy points, cyber tolerance score
- Attack forms with skill score, damage, and type
- Defenses (armor values for LI/HI/En)
- Complete skill list organized by Ability Score
- Gear list
- Cyber gear and mutations (if any)
- Background/behavior text description

Example character: Yatril Tor
STR 8 [+1], INT 12, DEX 11 [+1], WIL 11 [+1], CON 9, PER 11
Durability: 9/9/5/5 | Action check: 12+/11/5/2 | Move: sprint 18, run 12, walk 4 | #Actions: 2 | Reaction score: Ordinary/2
Perks: Tough as Nails, Psionic Awareness
Flaws: Bad Luck, Temper (moderate)
Psionic energy points: 6 | Cyber tolerance: 3/3/2
Attacks: Unarmed-brawl 9/4/2 d4s/d4+1s/d4+2s LI/O; 11mm ch pistol 12/6/3 d4+2w/d6+2w/d4+1m HI/O
Defenses: CF softsuit d6 (LI), d6 (HI), d6-1 (En)
Cyber gear: Cyberoptics
Mutations: Enhanced Intelligence, Wild Immune System

================================================================================
  #489 | SIDEBAR | GMG Page 258
  Back Cover Summary
================================================================================

Back cover text summarizing the Gamemaster Guide contents:
- Rules for creating memorable supporting characters, adventures, and campaigns for any SF setting.
- A "Fast-Play" chapter that teaches the basics of moderating the game and provides a starting adventure.
- Starship construction rules and a tactical space combat system.
- Comprehensive star system design rules, including stellar classes and planetary environments.
- More than 30 alien creatures and dangerous animals to use as opponents.
- Templates that quickly bring supporting characters to life.
- Guidelines for designing new alien species and alien artifacts.
- Adventure triggers to spur your imagination and ignite the action.
- A complete index for both the Player's Handbook and the Gamemaster Guide.
